Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Buyer's Option for Deficient Description Not Separately Priced
Ruling with proof on buyer's option when a described attribute is deficient but not part of the price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a missing description (wasf) not separately priced does not entitle the buyer to a price reduction, only to take the item at full price or cancel the sale, and distinguish this from cases where the attribute is part of the substance (asl) and commands a portion of the price.

Core Idea
A missing description does not reduce the price; the buyer must take it or leave it.

Imagine you buy a cloth described as 10 cubits for 10 dirhams. When it arrives, you find it is only 8 cubits. Can you demand a discount or must you pay the full price? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi answer: since the cubit is a description (wasf) and not a separate part of the price, you may either accept the cloth at the full price or cancel the sale — but you cannot reduce the price proportionally. This ruling hinges on a key distinction between descriptions that are intrinsic to the item and quantities that form the substance of the sale, such as grain measured by volume.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
State the scenario: buyer purchases cloth described as a certain length for a fixed price, then finds it shorter. The ruling is that the buyer has an option (khiyar): take the cloth at the full named price or cancel the sale. He cannot claim a proportional reduction.
This ruling is from the Hanafi school, as found in Al-Hidayah and other core texts.
2
Understand the Key Distinction: Wasf vs Asl
The cubit (dhirāʿ) is a description (wasf) of the cloth — it expresses length and width. In Hanafi law, a description that is not separately priced does not command any part of the price (thaman). By contrast, the substance (asl) of an item, such as the actual cloth or a quantity of grain, does command a portion of the price.
This distinction is central: if the attribute were part of the asl, deficiency would allow a price reduction.
3
Trace the Proof (Talil): Why No Price Reduction?
The reasoning is analogical: descriptions are like the limbs of an animal — no part of the price is allocated to them. Therefore, when only the description is deficient, the price remains unchanged. The buyer's option exists solely because the described attribute (waṣf) is missing, not because the price is reduced.
This is a form of qiyas: the cloth description is compared to animal limbs, both being attributes that do not command a share of the price.
4
Apply to Similar Cases and Exceptions
Contrast with the case of grain (sibra): here the quantity is the substance (asl), so if the quantity is less, the price is reduced proportionally. Also note the rule applies to land described by area. If the land is found larger, the excess belongs to the buyer (no option for seller) because it is an attribute.
This shows the scope: any attribute treated as a description (wasf) follows the same rule; only when the attribute is part of the substance does the rule differ.

Source Text

خریدا اس شرط پر کہ بائع نے کہا کہ یہ دس گز دس دراہم کے عوض ہے، اب اگر مشتری نے اس کو کم پایا مثلاً آٹھ گز ، تو اب مشتری کو اختیار ہے کہ یا تو پورے شمن کے ساتھ خرید لے یا چھوڑ دے، لیکن کم شمن کے ساتھ خریدنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ کپڑے میں گز وصف ہے اور وصف کے مقابلے میں ثمن نہیں آتا لہذ اگر کے مقابلے میں بھی شمن نہ ہوگا، جب وصف کے مقابلے میں شمن نہیں ہے تو اس کے فوت ہونے سے شمن میں کمی بھی نہیں ہوگی ، بر خلاف اصل کے کہ اس کے مقابلے میں شمن آئے گا، جیسے غلہ اور اناج کے مسئلے میں ، اگر اس میں کمی ہو تو شمن میں بھی کمی آئے گی۔

(الجوهرة النيرة كتاب البيوع، ج ۱ ص۱۸۷) (ومن اشترى ثوبا على أنه عشرة أذرع بعشرة دراهم) مثلا (أو أرضاً على أنها مائة ذراع بمائة درهم فوجدها أقل مما سمى له فالمشترى بالخيار إن شاء أخذها بجملة الثمن المسمى (وإن شاء تركها، لأن الذرع وصف في الثوب بخلاف الأول فإنه مقدار يقابله الثمن، والوصف لا يقابله شيء من الثمن، إلا أنه يخير لفوات الوصف المذكور وإن وجدها أكثر من الذراع الذي سماه البائع فهو) أى الزائد (للمشترى ولا خيار للبائع لما ذكرنا أنه صفة. اللباب في شرح الكتاب: كتاب البيوع، ج ۲ ص ۸)
الهداية كتاب البيوع، ج ۳ ص ۲
He bought it on condition that the seller said: This is ten cubits in exchange for ten dirhams. Then if the buyer finds it less, e.g., eight cubits, then the buyer has the option: either to buy it with the full price or to leave it, but he will not have the option to buy it with a reduced price. Because in the cloth the cubit is a description, and no part of the price is given in exchange for the description; thus when the description is lost, there is no reduction in the price. Contrary to the substance (asl), which commands a part of the price, as in the case of grain and food: if it is deficient, the price is also reduced. Because the cubit is a description in the cloth, as it is an expression of length and width, and no part of the price is given in exchange for the description, just like the limbs in an animal. Contrary to quantity in a heap (sibra), because a part of the price is given in exchange for the quantity. (Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 1, p. 187) (And whoever buys a cloth on condition that it is ten cubits for ten dirhams, for example, or land on condition that it is one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams, and finds it less than what was specified for him, then the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the entire named price, and if he wishes, he leaves it, because the cubit is a description in the cloth, unlike the first case where it is a quantity that commands a part of the price, and no part of the price is given in exchange for the description; however, he is given an option due to the loss of the mentioned description. And if he finds it more than the cubit which the seller specified, then it (i.e., the excess) belongs to the buyer, and the seller has no option, because we mentioned that it is an attribute. (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 2, p. 8) (Al-Hidaya, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 3, p. 2)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from classical Hanafi texts. It addresses the scenario where a buyer purchases a cloth described as a specific length (e.g., ten cubits) for a fixed price, but then finds it shorter. The author states that the cubit (dhirāʿ) is a description (waṣf) of the cloth, and in the absence of separate pricing per unit, the description does not command any part of the price (thaman). Therefore, the buyer cannot claim a proportional reduction; he may either accept the cloth with the full price or cancel the sale. The reasoning is that the price is paid for the substance of the cloth, not its attributes. An exception is when the subject matter is measured by weight or volume (like grain), where the quantity is an intrinsic part of the price and thus commands a corresponding portion of the price. The Arabic evidence from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira and al-Lubab supports this, emphasizing that the buyer's option arises due to the loss of the described attribute, not due to a price reduction. This ruling follows the Hanafi position that a non-separately-priced description does not entitle the buyer to a price abatement.

Key Terms
وصف (waṣf): Description or attribute of an item, such as the length (cubit) of a cloth, which is not an independent part of the price.
اصل (aṣl): Substance or core of an item, such as the cloth itself, which commands a part of the price.
ذراع (dhirāʿ): Cubit, a unit of length. In this context, an attribute of a cloth.
ثمن (thaman): Price, the monetary consideration for a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer purchases a cloth described as 10 cubits for 10 dirhams. He finds it is only 8 cubits. What are his legal options according to the Hanafi school?
A) He may take the cloth for 8 dirhams or cancel the sale.
B) He may take the cloth for the full 10 dirhams or cancel the sale.
C) He must cancel the sale because the description is not met.
D) He may demand 2 dirhams compensation.

Key Takeaway
A description (wasf) not separately priced does not command any part of the price; its deficiency gives the buyer only the option to accept the item at the full price or cancel the sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
When a Description Becomes Like the Principal in Sale
Legal maxim applied to a sale scenario

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a description (waṣf) is independently mentioned in the price, each unit is valued separately, and state the buyer's option when the goods are deficient.

Core Idea
A separately priced description transforms into a principal, entitling the buyer to a proportional reduction.

In previous lessons, we saw that a description attached to the sale object generally follows the principal. But there is a key exception: when the seller explicitly ties each unit of a description to a unit of price, that description becomes like a separate item. This lesson explains the scenario from Al-Hidayah where cloth is sold 'per cubit' at a fixed total. If the cloth is short, the buyer may take it at the reduced price or cancel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
The description (e.g., cubit) must be mentioned independently in exchange for a specific portion of the price, e.g., 'each cubit for one dirham'.
Without this independent price mention, the description remains subsidiary.
2
State the ruling
If the goods are found deficient, the buyer has the option to take them at a proportional price (e.g., 90 dirhams for 90 cubits) or cancel the sale.
The sale is valid, but the buyer has khiyar (option).
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
By independently pricing the description, each unit becomes like an independent principal (asl); therefore, the price is apportioned per unit.
This is a qiyas-like extension: each cubit is treated as a separate item of sale.
4
Distinguish from the general rule
Compare with the case where the description is not independently priced (e.g., '100 cubits for 100 dirhams' without per-unit price). In that case, deficiency only allows cancellation, not proportional reduction.
The key difference is the explicit mention of the price per unit of description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) الْوَصْفُ قَدْ يَكُونُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْأصْلِ بِإِفْرَادِهِ بِالذِّكْرِ .
ترجمہ: وصف الگ ذکر کرنے کی وجہ سے اصل کی طرح ہو جاتا ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر وصف کو الگ مستقل ثمن کے مقابلے میں ذکر کر دیا جائے تو یہ اصل کی مانند ہو جاتا ہے اور پھر اس کے مقابلے میں شمن آتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلار ہے ہیں کہ اگر بائع نے یہ کہا کہ میں اس سو گز کپڑے کو سو دراہم میں بیچتا ہوں، اس شرط پر کہ ہرگز ایک درہم کے عوض ہوگا، اب اگر مشتری نے اس کو کم پایا مثلاً نوے گز، تو اب مشتری کو اختیار ہے کہ یا تو نوے دراہم کے عوض لے لے یا چھوڑ دے۔ کیونکہ مذکورہ صورت میں بائع نے گز جو کہ وصف ہے ثمن کے مقابلے میں الگ ذکر کیا ہے اور وصف جب شمن کے مقابلے میں الگ ذکر کیا جائے تو وہ بمنزلہ اصل کے ہو جاتا ہے اور اصل کے مقابلے میں شمن آتا ہے، لہذا جتنا گز کپڑا ہو گا اتنی مقدار شمن ہوگا، جتنا گر کپڑا بڑھے گا اتفاثمن میں اضافہ ہوگا اور جتنا گر کپڑا کم ہوگا اتناشمن میں کمی ہوگی ، اس لیے کہ جب وصف کو الگ سے ذکر کیا تو یہ بمنزلہ اصل کے ہو گیا اور اصل کے ہر جز کے مقابل میں شمن آتا ہے۔
على أنها مائة ذراع بمائة درهم، كل ذراع بدرهم، فوجدها ناقصة، فالمشترى بالخيار إن شاء أخذها بحصتها من الثمن، وإن شاء ترك، لأن الوصف وإن كان تابعا لكنه صار أصلا بإفراده بذكر الثمن، فينزل كل ذراع منزلة ثوب وهذا معنى قولهم : إن الوصف يقابله شيء من الثمن، إذا كان مقصودا بالتناول البناية: كتاب البيوع، ج ۸ ص ٢٦) والأولى أن يقال : يعنى الأرض فإذا باعها على أنها مائة ذراع بمائة درهم كل ذراع بدرهم فإن وجدت ناقصة أخذها المشترى بحصتها من الثمن أو ترك، لأن الوصف وإن كان تابعا لكنه صار أصلا بإفراده بذكر الثمن فنزل كل ذراع بمنزلة ثوب العناية كتاب البيوع، ج ۶ ص ۲۷۳
(2) The description may become like the principal by being mentioned independently. Translation: The description becomes like the principal due to being separately mentioned. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that if the description is mentioned independently in exchange for the price, it becomes like the principal, and then a part of the price is given in exchange for it. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, informs that if the seller said: 'I sell this one hundred cubit cloth for one hundred dirhams, on condition that each cubit is in exchange for one dirham,' and the buyer finds it less, e.g., ninety cubits, then the buyer has the option: either to take it in exchange for ninety dirhams or to leave it. Because in the mentioned case, the seller mentioned the cubit, which is a description, independently in exchange for the price; and when the description is mentioned independently in exchange for the price, it becomes like the principal, and a part of the price is given in exchange for the principal; so whatever amount of cubits of cloth there is, the price will be that amount; if the cloth increases, the price increases; if the cloth decreases, the price decreases. Because when the description is mentioned separately, it becomes like the principal, and for every part of the principal, a part of the price is given. (Al-Binaya: Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 8, p. 26) And it is better to say: meaning land, if he sells it on condition that it is one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams, each cubit for a dirham, and he finds it deficient, the buyer takes it by its share of the price or leaves, because the description, though subsidiary, became a principal by being independently mentioned in exchange for the price, so each cubit is treated as a garment. (Al-Inaya: Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 6, p. 273)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents the second principle from Usool e Hidayah: a description (wasf) when mentioned independently in relation to the price attains the status of the principal (asl) and thus commands a part of the price. The author applies this to a scenario where the seller specifies each cubit at a dirham (e.g., 'one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams, each cubit for one dirham'). If the cloth is less, the buyer may take it at the proportional price (e.g., ninety dirhams for ninety cubits) or cancel. The reasoning is that by separately mentioning the description in connection with the price, each unit becomes akin to a separate item of sale, so deficiency in length proportionally reduces the price. The Arabic citations from al-Binaya and al-Inaya confirm this. This rule is distinct from the previous one: here, the buyer can take the goods at a reduced price, while in the previous case he could only take all or leave.

Key Terms
وصف (waṣf): Description (e.g., cubit) that, when separately mentioned in relation to the price, becomes like the principal and commands a part of the price.
اصل (aṣl): The principal substance; when a description becomes like the asl, each unit is valued separately.
شفع (shufʿa): Not directly used, but related to proportional sharing in some contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A seller says: 'I sell this 100-cubit cloth for 100 dirhams, each cubit for 1 dirham.' The buyer finds it is 90 cubits. According to the Hanafi school, what are the buyer's options?
A) He must take the cloth for 100 dirhams or cancel.
B) He may take it for 90 dirhams or cancel.
C) He may only cancel the sale.
D) He may take it for 100 dirhams and demand compensation.

Key Takeaway
When a description is independently mentioned in exchange for a portion of the price, it becomes like a principal, allowing the buyer to pay proportionally or cancel.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Sale with Per-Unit Pricing: Buyer's Option on Deficiency
Explaining the ruling and its rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a sold item is found deficient in quantity after a per-unit price was specified, and explain the legal rationale that transforms the description into a principal.

Core Idea
When a description is separately priced, it becomes like the principal itself – each unit corresponds to a portion of the price.

In Hanafi sales law, when a seller specifies a per-unit price for a quantity, the contract creates a unique linkage between each unit and a portion of the total price. If the quantity is deficient, the buyer is not forced to pay the full price for less. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the subtle principle that a description, when explicitly paired with the price, elevates from being subordinate to becoming a principal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract scenario
The seller states a specific total quantity and total price, adding that each unit (e.g., yard) has a separate price. For example: '100 yards for 100 dirhams, each yard for a dirham.'
The key is the separate mention of per-unit price.
2
Determine the ruling on deficiency
If the buyer finds the cloth less than stated (e.g., 90 yards instead of 100), the buyer has an option (khiyar): either take the cloth at a proportional reduced price (90 dirhams) or cancel the sale entirely.
The option belongs solely to the buyer, not the seller.
3
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The description (yard) when separately mentioned with the price becomes like an independent principal (asl). Just as each garment from a heap is priced individually, each yard now corresponds to a fraction of the total price.
The principle: 'al-wasf idha ufrida bi dhikr al-thaman yasiru aslan' (description separately mentioned with price becomes principal).
4
Apply the principle to similar cases
The same ruling applies to land sold as '100 square meters for 1000 dirhams, each square meter for 10 dirhams.' If only 80 sq. meters are delivered, the buyer may take at 800 dirhams or cancel.
The illa (effective cause) is the separate pricing of each unit.
5
Distinguish from non-separate pricing
If the seller simply says 'this cloth is 100 dirhams' without per-unit price, a deficiency in quantity does not create an option; the buyer may claim damages or cancel for misrepresentation, but not take at a proportional reduction automatically.
The difference lies in the explicit pairing of each unit with a price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذکر کر دیا جائے تو یہ اصل کی مانند ہو جاتا ہے اور پھر اس کے مقابلے میں ثمن آتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر بائع نے یہ کہا کہ میں اس سو گز کپڑے کو سو دراہم میں بیچتا ہوں، اس شرط پر کہ ہر گز ایک درہم کے عوض ہوگا، اب اگر مشتری نے اس کو کم پایا مثلاً نوے گز، تو اب مشتری کو اختیار ہے کہ یا تو نوے دراہم کے عوض لے لے یا چھوڑ دے۔ کیونکہ مذکورہ صورت میں بائع نے گز جو کہ وصف ہے ثمن کے مقابلے میں الگ ذکر کیا ہے اور وصف جب ثمن کے مقابلے میں الگ ذکر کیا جائے تو وہ بمنزلہ اصل کے ہو جاتا ہے اور اصل کے مقابلے میں ثمن آتا ہے، لہذا جتنا گز کپڑا ہو گا اتنی مقدار ثمن ہوگا، جتنا کپڑا بڑھے گا اثمن میں اضافہ ہوگا اور جتنا کپڑا کم ہوگا اتنا ثمن میں کمی ہوگی، اس لیے کہ جب وصف کو الگ سے ذکر کیا تو یہ بمنزلہ اصل کے ہو گیا اور اصل کے ہر جز کے مقابل میں ثمن آتا ہے۔

على أنها مائة ذراع بمائة درهم، كل ذراع بدرهم، فوجدها ناقصة، فالمشترى بالخيار إن شاء أخذها بحصتها من الثمن، وإن شاء ترك، لأن الوصف وإن كان تابعا لكنه صار أصلا بإفراده بذكر الثمن، فينزل كل ذراع منزلة ثوب وهذا معنى قولهم : إن الوصف يقابله شيء من الثمن، إذا كان مقصودا بالتناول (البناية: كتاب البيوع، ج 8 ص 26) والأولى أن يقال : يعني الأرض فإذا باعها على أنها مائة ذراع بمائة درهم كل ذراع بدرهم فإن وجدت ناقصة أخذها المشترى بحصتها من الثمن أو ترك، لأن الوصف وإن كان تابعا لكنه صار أصلا بإفراده بذكر الثمن فنزل كل ذراع بمنزلة ثوب (العناية: كتاب البيوع، ج 6 ص 273)
If he says: 'It is 100 yards for 100 dirhams, each yard for a dirham,' and finds it less, then the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes it at its proportional price; if he wishes, he leaves it. Because the description, although subordinate, becomes a principal by its separate mention with the price, so each yard is treated like a garment. This is the meaning of their statement: 'The description is matched by a portion of the price when it is intended by the transaction.' (Al-Binayah, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 8 p. 26) And it is better to say: meaning land, if he sells it on the basis that it is 100 yards for 100 dirhams, each yard for a dirham, and he finds it less, the buyer takes it at its proportional price or leaves it, because the description, although subordinate, becomes a principal by its separate mention with the price, so each yard is treated like a garment. (Al-Inayah, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 6 p. 273)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage explains a key principle in Hanafi sales law. The ruling is: if a seller sells a specific quantity of cloth at a specific total price, but with the condition that each unit (yard) has a separate price, then if the buyer finds the quantity deficient, he has the option (khiyar) to either take the cloth at a reduced price proportional to the deficiency or cancel the sale entirely. The rationale (ta'lil) is that when the seller explicitly mentions the description (the per-unit price) alongside the price, that description becomes like the principal (asl) itself. Just as the principal item corresponds to the price, each unit of the description now corresponds to a portion of the price. Therefore, the price is adjusted proportionally to the quantity received. This is a specific application of the general rule that a description, when made independent by being paired with the price, takes the status of the principal. The text cites Al-Hidayah and Al-Inayah to confirm this as part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
وصف (waṣf): The description or attribute of the sold item, here the per-unit price per yard.
ثمن (thaman): The price or consideration in a sale contract.
أصل (aṣl): The principal item or the independent entity against which the price is measured.
تبع (tabaʿ): Subordinate or dependent; the description is normally subordinate to the principal item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, when the buyer finds the cloth deficient (e.g., 90 yards instead of 100), what is the buyer's correct legal position?
A) The buyer must accept the cloth at the full price of 100 dirhams.
B) The buyer may accept the cloth at a proportional price of 90 dirhams or cancel the sale.
C) The buyer must accept the cloth at 90 dirhams—no option to cancel.
D) The sale is automatically void (batil).

Key Takeaway
When a per-unit price is explicitly stated, each unit becomes a principal item, and any deficiency gives the buyer an option to take the remainder at a proportional price or rescind.

Absolute Words Interpreted According to Custom: Sale of House Includes Building
Ruling with proof: applying customary interpretation to a sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of customary interpretation (al-mutlaq yunsarif ila al-mutafahim fi al-urf) to determine what is included in a sale when only an absolute term is used.

Core Idea
Absolute words are interpreted by custom; selling a 'house' includes the building automatically.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi contract law: absolute terms in a sale are understood according to common custom. The author of Al-Hidayah exemplifies this by ruling that selling a 'dar' (house) automatically includes the building – roof and walls – even if not mentioned. Understanding this principle is fundamental for correctly interpreting sale contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the absolute term
Look at the contract language: was the word 'dar' used without any qualification? If so, it is an absolute term.
Absolute means no restrictions like 'without building'.
2
Determine the customary meaning
Consult the local custom ('urf): what does 'dar' conventionally include? In the Hanafi context, it includes both land and the building attached to it.
Custom must be widespread and stable.
3
Apply the principle
Since custom includes the building, the absolute term 'dar' is interpreted accordingly, so the building is part of the sale.
This is based on the general usul rule: al-mutlaq yunsarif ila al-mutafahim fi al-urf.
4
Recognize the rationale
The building is permanently attached to the land (ittisal qarar), so it naturally follows the land as subordinate.
If the building were temporary or separate, different rules might apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل من باع دارا دخل بناؤه في البيع

(۷) الْمُطْلَقُ مِنَ الْأَلْفَاظِ يَنْصَرِفْ إِلَى الْمُتَفَاهَمِ فِي الْعُرُفِ. ترجمہ: مطلق الفاظ ان معانی کی طرف پھیر دیے جائیں گے جو عرف میں ان سے سمجھے جاتے ہوں۔

تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب الفاظ مطلق ذکر ہوں تو ان سے وہی معانی مراد ہوں گے جو عرف میں ان سے سمجھے جاتے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر ایک آدمی نے دوسرے پر گھر فروخت کیا تو چھت اور دیوار میں بھی بیچ میں داخل ہوں گی اگر چہ بائع نے اس کا ذکر نہ کیا ہو، کیونکہ بائع نے "دار" کا لفظ مطلق بولا ہے اور مطلق لفظ کو اس معنی کی طرف پھیرا جاتا ہے جو عرف میں اس سے مراد لیتے ہیں، لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں بھی "دار" کے لفظ سے وہی مراد ہوگا جو عرف میں متفاہم ہے اور عرف میں دار سے چھت اور دیوار سمیت گھر مراد ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہاں بھی دار سے چھت اور دیوار سمیت گھر مراد ہوگا۔ اس لیے کہ عرف میں دار عمارت سے آراستہ زمین کو کہتے ہیں، ورنہ عمارت سے خالی جگہ صحراء اور میدان کہلاتی ہے۔

(الهداية: كتاب البيوع، ج 3 ص 26) البناء في عقد البيع، لأن اسم الدار يتناول العرصة والبناء في العرف، وهو متصل به اتصال قرار، فيدخل تبعا له، والأصل في جنس هذا أن كل ما كان اسم المبيع متناولا له عرفا أو كان متصلا به اتصال قرار وهو ما وضع لا ليفصل دخل من غير ذكر (اللباب في شرح الكتاب: كتاب البيوع، ج 2 ص 9) قوله ومن باع دارا دخل بناؤها في البيع وإن لم يسمه) لأن اسم الدار يتناول
Section: Whoever sells a house, its building enters into the sale. (7) Absolute words are turned to what is understood in custom. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that when words are mentioned in absolute terms, then their meanings are taken according to what is understood in custom. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is explaining that if a person sells a house to another, then the roof and walls are included in the sale even if the seller did not mention them, because the seller uttered the word 'dar' absolutely, and an absolute word is turned to the meaning that is understood in custom. So in this case, the word 'dar' means what is customarily understood, and customarily 'dar' refers to a house including the roof and walls. Thus, here too, 'dar' means the house including the roof and walls. This is because in custom, 'dar' is called land adorned with a building; otherwise, land without a building is called a desert or field. (Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 3 p. 26) The building in the contract of sale, because the name 'dar' includes the plot and the building in custom, and it is attached to it with a stable attachment, so it enters as subordinate. The principle in this type is that everything which the name of the sold item includes customarily, or is attached to it with a stable attachment in a way that it is placed not to be separated, enters without mention. (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 2 p. 9) His statement: 'Whoever sells a house, its building enters into the sale even if he does not name it' because the name 'dar' includes.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental rule in Hanafi fiqh: absolute words (mutlaq) are interpreted according to their customary understanding (al-mutafahim fi al-urf). The author applies this to the sale of a house (dar). In custom, the word 'dar' includes the building (bina'), roof (saqf), and walls (jidaar). Therefore, when someone sells a 'dar', all these components are automatically included in the sale without explicit mention. This is because the building is physically attached (ittisal qarar) in a permanent way. The text also cites Al-Hidayah and Al-Lubab to support that if an item's name covers something customarily or it is permanently attached, it is included by default. This principle ensures that sale contracts are interpreted in line with common commercial practices. The ruling is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah and the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مطلق (muṭlaq): An unqualified word without any restriction or specification.
عرف (ʿurf): Custom or common usage that determines the meaning of absolute terms.
دار (dār): A house, which in custom includes the land (plot) and the building (structure).
بناء (bināʾ): The building or structure attached to the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only the land (plot).
B) The land and the building, including roof and walls.
C) Only the building, not the land.
D) Nothing is included until explicitly stated.

Key Takeaway
When a word is used absolutely in a contract, its meaning is determined by custom; selling a 'house' includes the building automatically.

Principle of Iltisal Qarar: What Enters a Sale Automatically
States principle that permanently attached items are included in sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ittisal qarar to determine whether attached items (trees, crops, fruits) are automatically included in a sale of land.

Core Idea
Permanently attached items enter the sale; temporary attachments do not.

In Hanafi sales law, what exactly is included when you buy land? This lesson unpacks the key principle from Al-Hidayah: objects attached to the land with a connection intended for stability (ittisal qarar) are automatically part of the sale. You will learn to distinguish between trees (included) and crops or fruits (excluded without mention), and understand the qiyas that supports this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
The text states: 'Whatever is connected with a connection of stability enters in the sale.' Understand that 'stability' (qarar) means the attachment is meant to be permanent, not temporary.
2
Distinguish Between Permanent and Temporary Attachments
Trees are attached for stability; crops are attached for harvest (separation). The legal effect depends on this nature.
3
Apply Qiyas to Understand the Rule
Trees are analogized to a building on a house; crops are analogized to movable furnishings. The underlying cause (illa) is the purpose of the connection.
4
Extend the Principle to Fruits
Fruits on a tree are not included even when the tree itself is sold, because fruits are meant for cutting, not remaining.
5
Summarize the Practical Outcome
When buying land, trees are included by default; crops and fruits require explicit mention. This prevents disputes and uncertainty (gharar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَا كَانَ مُتَّصِلا بِالْمَبِيعِ اتِّصَالَ قَرَارٍ يَدْخُلُ فِى الْبَيْعِ. (الهداية: كتاب البيوع، ج ٣ ص ٢٦) وَيَدْخُلُ الشَّجَرُ) وَإِنْ لَمْ يُسَمِّهِ (لَا الزَّرْعُ إِلَّا بِالتَّسْمِيَةِ (بِشِرَاءِ الْأَرْضِ) لِأَنَّ الشَّجَرَ مُتَصِلٌ بِهَا لِلْقَرَارِ فَأَشْبَهَ الْبِنَاءَ، وَالزَّرْعُ مُتَّصِلٌ بِهِ لِلْفَصْلِ فَأَشْبَهَ مَتَاعًا فِيهَا وَلَا الثَّمَرُ بِشِرَاءِ شَجَرَةٍ لِأَنَّ الأَنْصَالَ، وَإِنْ كَانَ خِلْقِيًّا فَهُوَ لِلْقَطْعِ لَا لِلْبَقَاءِ فَصَارَ
Whatever is connected to the sold item with a connection of stability enters in the sale. (Al-Hidayah: Book of Sales, vol. 3 p. 26) And the trees enter (even if he does not name them), but not the crops except by naming (in the purchase of land), because the trees are connected to it for stability, so they resemble the building; and the crops are connected to it for separation, so they resemble furnishings in it; and not the fruits by purchase of a tree, because the roots, even if they are natural, are for cutting, not for remaining, so it becomes...
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage introduces the eighth principle: any item attached to the sold property for stability (ittisal qarar) is automatically included in the sale. The key distinction lies in the purpose of attachment. Trees planted in land are attached for permanence, so they are included when land is sold, just like a building on a house. Crops (zurr), however, are attached only temporarily for harvesting; they are like movable furnishings (mata') and are not included unless explicitly mentioned. Similarly, fruits on a tree are not included when selling a tree because they are meant for cutting, not remaining. The proof is from Al-Hidayah, using analogy (qiyas): trees are analogous to buildings (both for stability), while crops are analogous to movable goods (both for separation). This principle ensures clarity in sales of land and real estate.

Key Terms
اتصال قرار (ittisal qarar): A connection intended for permanence and stability, such that separation would cause harm to the main item.
شجر (shajar): Trees planted for long-term growth, attached to land for stability.
زرع (zar'): Crops planted for seasonal harvest, attached temporarily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Both trees and crops are included.
B) Only the trees are included; crops are not.
C) Only the crops are included; trees are not.
D) Neither trees nor crops are included.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of ittisal qarar ensures that permanently attached items (trees) are automatically included in a land sale, while temporary attachments (crops, fruits) are not unless specified.

Attachments of Permanence in Sale
States a fiqh principle and proves it via qiyas jali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ittisal qarar to determine whether an attached item is automatically included in a sale of land or property.

Core Idea
Any item attached for permanence enters the sale; any item attached for separation does not.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a foundational principle in Hanafi sales law: the distinction between permanent attachments (ittisal qarar) and temporary attachments (ittisal fasl). The ruling determines what is automatically transferred with the sale of land without explicit mention, preventing uncertainty. We will unpack the principle, its analogical proof, and its practical applications.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Read the Arabic text: 'ما كان متصلا بالمبيع اتصال قرار يدخل في البيع'. Understand that any item attached to the sold item in a way that implies permanence (separation would damage the main object) is included in the sale automatically.
This is a general rule derived from custom and analogy.
2
Identify the two categories
Distinguish between ittisal qarar (attachment for permanence, e.g., building, trees) and ittisal fasl (attachment for separation, e.g., crops, fruit). The former enters the sale; the latter does not unless specified.
The key criterion: is the attachment intended for stability or for eventual removal?
3
Analyze the proof via qiyas
The text uses qiyas jali (clear analogy): trees on land are analogous to a building on a courtyard. Both are permanently attached and integral to the land. The illa (effective cause) is ittisal qarar. Crops are analogous to household goods because they are separable.
The building enters sale by custom and necessity; trees follow the same logic.
4
Apply the principle to new cases
Practice with scenarios: a house sold with a built-in wardrobe (permanent, included) vs. a freestanding cupboard (not included). Fruit on a tree is not included because it is intended for picking (separation).
Always check the nature of attachment and custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸) مَا كَانَ مُتَّصِلا بِالْمَبِيعِ اتِّصَالَ قَرَارٍ يَدْخُلُ فِى الْبَيْعِ . ترجمہ: ہر وہ چیز جو مبیع کے ساتھ متصل ہوا سے برقرار رکھنے کے لیے تو وہ بیع میں داخل ہوگی۔ تشریح مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو شے بھی مبیع کے ساتھ ایسی متصل ہو کہ اس کو الگ کرنے میں مبیع میں فساد آتا ہو تو یہ شے بھی مبیع کے تابع ہو کر بیچ میں داخل ہو گی اگر چہ بائع نے اس کا ذکر نہ کیا ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے ایسی زمین فروخت کی جس پر درخت لگے ہوئے تھے، تو بیچ میں یہ درخت بھی داخل ہوں گے اگر چہ بائع نے اس کا ذکر نہ کیا ہو، اس لیے کہ زمین کے ساتھ درخت کا اتصال، اتصال قرار ہے اور ہر وہ شے جو کسی چیز کے ساتھ متصل ہو اسے برقرار رکھنے کے لیے تو وہ بغیر کسی وضاحت کے بھی بیع میں داخل ہوتی ہے، جس طرح بیچ دار میں عمارت شامل ہوتی ہے، اسی طرح بیع ارض میں درخت بھی شامل ہوں گے، البتہ کھیتی زمین کی بیچ میں شامل نہ ہوگی جب تک کہ اس کی صراحت نہ کرے، اس لیے کہ کھیتی کا زمین سے اتصال، اتصال قرار نہیں ہے، وہ زمین سے جدا ہونے کے لیے متصل ہے، تو یہ گھر میں موجود سامان کے مشابہ ہے، جس طرح گھر کی بیع میں سامان شامل نہیں ہوتا ، اسی طرح زمین کی بیع میں کھیتی شامل نہیں ہوگی، الا یہ کہ وہ اس کی صراحت کر دے۔
العرصة والبناء فى العرف لأنه متصل بها اتصال قرار ولأن البناء في الدار من صفاتها وصفات المبيع تابعة له الجوهرة النيرة كتاب البيوع، ج ۱ ص ۱۸۸) الهداية كتاب البيوع، ج ۳ ص ۲۶
وَيَدْخُلُ الشَّجَرُ) وَإِنْ لَمْ يُسَمِّهِ (لَا الزَّرُعُ إِلَّا بِالتَّسْمِيَةِ (بِشِرَاءِ الْأَرْضِ) لِأَنَّ الشَّجَرَ مُتَصِلٌ بِهَا لِلْقَرَارِ فَأَشْبَهَ الْبِنَاءَ، وَالزَّرْعُ مُتَّصِلٌ بِهِ لِلْفَصْلِ فَأَشْبَهَ مَتَاعًا فِيهَا وَلَا الثَّمَرُ بِشِرَاءِ شَجَرَةٍ لِأَنَّ الأَنْصَالَ، وَإِنْ كَانَ خِلْقِيًّا فَهُوَ لِلْقَطْعِ لَا لِلْبَقَاءِ فَصَارَ
Principle (8): Whatever is attached to the sold item with an attachment of permanence enters into the sale. Translation: Every item that is attached to the sold item for the purpose of stability enters the sale. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that any item attached to the sold item in such a way that separating it would cause damage to the sold item also enters the sale as subordinate to the sold item, even if the seller did not mention it. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if someone sold land on which trees were planted, the trees are included in the sale even if the seller did not mention them, because the attachment of trees to the land is an attachment of stability. And every item attached to something for its stability enters the sale without specification, just as a building is included in the sale of a house. Similarly, trees are included in the sale of land. However, crops are not included in the sale of land unless specified, because the attachment of crops to the land is not an attachment of stability; they are attached for the purpose of separation. Thus they resemble household goods in a house; just as household goods are not included in the sale of a house, crops are not included in the sale of land unless specified. (Then Arabic quote from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and Al-Hidayah): The courtyard and the building are customarily considered attached to it with an attachment of permanence, and because the building is among the qualities of the house, and qualities of the sold item are subordinate to it. (Al-Hidayah, Book of Sales, vol. 3 p. 26) And the tree enters (into the sale) even if he did not name it; but not the crop unless by naming it (in the purchase of land) because the tree is attached to it for permanence, so it resembles the building; and the crop is attached to it for separation, so it resembles goods in it. And fruit does not enter with the purchase of a tree because even if it is natural, it is for cutting, not for remaining; thus it becomes...
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents an important Hanafi principle governing inclusions in sales: attachments of permanence (ittisal qarar) automatically enter the sale, while attachments for separation (ittisal fasl) do not. The commentator opens by stating the principle in Arabic, then provides a Urdu explanation. The principle is applied to land sales: trees on land are included because they are permanently attached and removing them would damage the land; crops, however, are not included unless mentioned because they are planted for eventual harvest and separation. The commentator draws an analogy: trees are like buildings (both are permanent fixtures), while crops are like household goods (temporary and separable). The passage then quotes from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and Al-Hidayah to reinforce the ruling, noting that customary practice also treats buildings and the courtyard as part of the house. The Hidayah quote adds that fruit on a tree is also not included when buying the tree because fruit, even if naturally occurring, is intended for picking, not for remaining. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi sales law: buyers and sellers must be aware of what is automatically transferred and what requires explicit mention.

Key Terms
اتصال قرار (ittisal qarar): Attachment of permanence: an attachment intended for stability, such that separating the item would damage the main object or alter its nature.
اتصال فصل (ittisal fasl): Attachment for separation: a temporary attachment intended for eventual removal, without causing damage to the main object upon separation.
مبیع (mabī‘): The sold item; the subject matter of a sale contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Crops growing on the land
B) Trees planted on the land
C) Furniture inside a house on the land
D) Harvested grain stored on the land

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sale automatically transfers all items attached for permanence (ittisal qarar) but not those attached for separation (ittisal fasl).

Principle: Invalidating Conditions in Sale
States that any condition not required by the contract renders the sale void (fasid).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an invalid condition (shart fasid) in a sale contract and state that it renders the sale fasid by applying the Hanafi criterion of opposition to muqtada al-'aqd.

Core Idea
A condition that contradicts the contract's essential purpose invalidates the sale.

This lesson introduces a fundamental Hanafi rule: any condition that contradicts the inherent requirement of a sale contract (muqtada al-'aqd) makes the sale fasid. Understanding this principle helps distinguish valid stipulations from invalid ones, using the classic example of buying fruit on a tree with a condition to leave it until ripe.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition in the sale
Find the specific stipulation added by one party to the sale agreement.
Example: 'I buy the fruit on the tree but they must stay until ripe.'
2
Determine muqtada al-'aqd
Recall the essential obligations the contract imposes by its nature: immediate transfer of ownership, delivery of the sold item, and payment of price.
The sale's purpose is to clear liability of both parties immediately.
3
Compare condition to muqtada al-'aqd
Check if the condition opposes or delays the fulfillment of any essential obligation.
Condition to leave fruit on tree prevents immediate delivery, opposing muqtada al-'aqd.
4
Conclude the ruling
If the condition contradicts muqtada al-'aqd, it is a shart fasid and the sale becomes fasid. The sale can be rectified by removing the condition.
The sale is not batil; it is fasid and can be corrected.

(۹) كُلُّ شَرْطٍ لَا يَقْتَضِيهِ الْعَقْدُ فَهُوَ مُفْسِدٌ لِلْبَيْعِ . ترجمہ: ہر ایسی شرط جس کا عقد تقاضانہ کرے تو وہ بیع کو فاسد کرتی ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بیع شرط فاسد سے فاسد ہو جاتی ہے اور ہر ایسی شرط لگانا جو مقتضی عقد کے خلاف ہودہ شرط فاسد کہلاتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے درخت کے اوپر پھل خریدے اور پھر مشتری نے یہ شرط لگائی کہ جب تک پھل پک نہ جائیں یہ درخت پر ہی ہوں گے تو بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ مشتری نے جو مذکورہ شرط لگائی ہے یہ مقتضائے عقد کے خلاف ہے، اور ہر ایسی شرط جو مقتضائے عقد کے خلاف ہو، اس سے بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے، اس لیے بیع مکمل ہونے کے بعد ضروری ہے کہ بائع مشتری کو مبیع حوالے کرے اور مشتری بائع کوشن سپر د کرے، اب پھلوں کو درخت پر چھوڑنے کی شرط لگانے کی صورت میں میچ بائع کی ملکیت کے ساتھ مشغول ہوگی اور فراغ ذمہ نہیں ہوگا ، اور عقد کا مقتضی یہ ہے کہ اتمام عقد کے بعد بائع صحیح اور مشتری ثمن سپرد کر کے عقد ذمہ سے فارغ ہو جائیں، اب پھلوں کو درخت پر چھوڑنے کی شرط لگانے سے عقد ذمہ سے فراغت نہیں ہوگی ، تو یہ شرط كَالزَّرْع. درر الحكام كتاب البيوع، ج ۲ ص ۱۵۰)
ومن باع أرضا دخل ما فيها من النخل والشجر وإن لم يسمه لأنه أى لأن الشجر (متصل به) أى بالأرض على تأويل المكان (للقرار فأشبه البناء) فيكون تبعا له ولا يدخل الزرع فى بيع الأرض إلا بالتسمية لأنه أى لأن الزرع (متصل به أى بالأرض (للفصل) يعنى ليس اتصاله للتأبيد، ولرفعه غاية معلومة فشابه المتاع الذي فيها أى فى الأرض فلم يدخل في المبيع إلا بالشرط.
(العناية : كتاب البيوع، ج۸ ص ۳۲)
الهداية كتاب البيوع، ج ۳ ص۲۷
Principle (9): Every condition that the contract does not require is invalidating for the sale. Translation: Every condition that the contract does not necessitate invalidates the sale. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that a sale becomes invalid due to an invalid condition, and every condition that opposes the requirement of the contract is called an invalid condition. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if someone bought fruit on a tree and then the buyer stipulated that the fruit should remain on the tree until it ripens, the sale becomes invalid, because the condition imposed by the buyer is against the requirement of the contract, and every condition opposed to the requirement of the contract invalidates the sale. Therefore, after the completion of the sale, it is necessary for the seller to hand over the sold item to the buyer and for the buyer to hand over the price to the seller. Now, by stipulating to leave the fruit on the tree, the sold item will remain occupied with the seller's ownership and the liability will not be cleared. And the requirement of the contract is that after the completion of the contract, the seller clears his liability by delivering the sold item and the buyer by paying the price. So by stipulating to leave the fruit on the tree, clearing of liability does not occur; thus this condition is like crops. (Durar al-Hukkam, Book of Sales, vol. 2 p. 150) And whoever sells land, whatever is in it of date palms and trees enters (the sale) even if he did not name them, because the trees are attached to the land with an attachment of permanence, thus resembling the building, and they become subordinate to it. And crops do not enter in the sale of land except by naming, because crops are attached to the land for separation, meaning their attachment is not for permanence; rather they have a known end for removal, so they resemble the goods in the land, and thus they do not enter the sold item except by condition. (Al-Inayah, Book of Sales, vol. 8 p. 32) (Al-Hidayah, Book of Sales, vol. 3 p. 27).
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage introduces another crucial principle of Hanafi sales law: any condition that is not necessitated by the contract (i.e., that contradicts its essential purpose) renders the sale fasid (invalid). The commentator begins by stating the principle in Arabic, then provides an Urdu explanation. The key example given is buying fruit on a tree with a condition that the fruit remain on the tree until ripe. The purpose of a sale is immediate transfer of ownership and possession: the seller must deliver the sold item, and the buyer must pay the price. By stipulating that the fruit stay on the tree, the buyer prevents the seller from clearing his liability, as the fruit remains in the seller's tree. This condition is contrary to the contract's requirement (muqtada al-'aqd), so the sale is fasid. The passage then quotes from Durar al-Hukkam, which compares this condition to crops (which are also not included automatically). The subsequent Arabic quotes from Al-Inayah and Al-Hidayah reiterate the earlier principle about inclusions, reinforcing that trees are included automatically (as they are permanently attached) but crops require explicit condition. This connection shows the coherence of Hanafi fiqh: the same reasoning about attachment types governs both inclusion and exclusion of conditions.

Key Terms
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): An invalid condition that contradicts the requirement of the contract and thereby renders the sale fasid.
مقتضى العقد (muqtada al-'aqd): The inherent requirement of the contract; the essential obligations that the contract imposes by its nature, such as immediate delivery of the sold item and payment of price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best explains why a condition that fruit remain on tree until ripe invalidates the sale under Hanafi law?
A) The buyer does not have immediate possession.
B) The condition contradicts the requirement of immediate transfer of ownership and liability clearance.
C) The fruit is not owned by the seller.
D) The seller has no control over ripening.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a condition in a sale depends on whether it opposes the contract's inherent purpose; any such condition renders the sale fasid.

Inability to Deliver: The Hanafi Principle Invalidating Sales
Explaining the second principle regarding delivery impossibility in sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that inability to deliver invalidates a sale, apply it to a scenario with a condition preventing delivery, and explain the underlying proof from the prohibition of safqa fi safqa.

Core Idea
If the seller cannot physically hand over the sold item at contract time, the sale is fasid — ruled invalid by the Prophet's ban on a transaction within a transaction.

This lesson presents a fundamental principle in Hanafi sales law: ta'addur taslim al-mabee' yufsid al-bay'. We will examine how a condition that prevents delivery — such as requiring fruit to remain on the tree — turns the sale into a prohibited double contract. The discussion draws from Bada'i' al-Sana'i', Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and al-Hidayah, demonstrating the meticulous reasoning that makes Hanafi fiqh a highly structured legal system.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its key term
Ta'addur taslim al-mabee' means inability of the seller to deliver the sold item. This principle declares that a sale is fasid if such inability exists at the time of contract.
2
Examine the example provided
Buying fruit with a condition that it remains on the tree. Why does this prevent delivery? Because the seller retains possession.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The condition is not required by the contract, benefits only the seller, and is not customary. It leads to a double transaction (safqa fi safqa): the sale plus an implied hire or loan of the tree.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'nahaa 'an safqatin fi safqa' prohibits combining two transactions in one. This hadith is cited to show the condition violates a clear prophetic prohibition.
5
Connect to the Hanafi ruling
The sale is classified as fasid (voidable), not batil (void), because the defect is in an external condition, not in the essential pillars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٠) تَعَدرُ تَسليم المبيع يُفْسِدُ البَيْعَ .
ترجمہ بیج کا حوالہ کرنا مستعذ رہو تو یہ بیع کو فاسد کرتا ہے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس صورت میں مبیع کا مشتری کے سپرد کرنا وَإِنْ اشْتَرَى بِشَرْطِ التَّرْكِ، فَالْعَقْدُ فَاسِدٌ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ، لِأَنَّهُ شَرُطٌ لَا يَقْتَضِيهِ الْعَقْدُ وَفِيهِ مَنْفَعَةٌ لِأَحَدِ الْمُتَعَاقِدَيْنِ وَلَا يُلَائِمُ الْعَقْدَ وَلَا جَرَى بِهِ التَّعَامُلُ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ، وَمِثْلُ هَذَا الشَّرْطِ مُفْسِدَّ لِلْبَيْعِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَلَأَنَّهُ لَا يَتَمَكَّنُ مِنْ التَّرْكِ إِلَّا بِإِعَارَةِ الشَّجَرَةِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَهُمَا مِلْكُ الْبَائِعِ فَصَارَ بِشَرْطِ التَّرْكِ شَارِطًا الْإِعَارَةَ فَكَانَ شَرُطُهُ صَفْقَةٌ فِى صَفْقَةٍ وَإِنَّهُ مَنْهِيٌّ . (بدائع الصنائع: كتاب البيوع، فصل في شرائط الصحة في البيع، ج ۵ ص ۱۷۳)
قَالَ (وَإِنْ شَرَطَ تَرَكَهَا عَلَى النَّخْلِ فَسَدَ أَى الْبَيْعُ لِأَنَّهُ شَرُطُ لَا يَقْتَضِيهِ الْعَقْدُ وَهُوَ شُغْلُ مِلْكِ الْغَيْرِ أَوْ نَقُولُ إِنَّهُ صَفْقَةٌ فِي صَفْقَةٍ، لِأَنَّهُ إِجَارَةٌ فِي بَيْعِ إِنْ كَانَ لِلْمَنْفَعَةِ حِصَّةٌ مِنْ الثَّمَنِ أَوْ إِعَارَةٌ فِي بَيْعِ إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهَا حِصَّةٌ مِنْ الشَّمَنِ وَقَدْ نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنْ صَفْقَةٍ فِي صَفْقَةٍ. (تبيين الحقائق: كتاب البيوع، فصل يدخل البناء والمفاتيح في بيع، ج ۴ ص ۱۲)
الهداية كتاب البيوع، ج ۳ ص ۲۸
(10) Inability to deliver the sold item invalidates the sale. Translation: If delivering the sold item becomes difficult, it invalidates the sale. Elaboration: The meaning of the above principle is that when the sold item cannot be handed over to the buyer... And if he buys with a condition of leaving, the contract is invalid by consensus, because it is a condition not necessitated by the contract, and it contains a benefit for one of the contracting parties, does not harmonize with the contract, and is not customary among people. Such a condition invalidates the sale for the reasons we mentioned, and because he cannot leave the fruit except by loaning the tree and land, which are the property of the seller. Thus, by stipulating leaving, he is stipulating a loan, so his condition is a transaction within a transaction, which is prohibited. (Bada'i' al-Sana'i': Book of Sales, Chapter on Conditions of Validity in Sale, vol. 5, p. 173) He said: And if he stipulates leaving them on the date palms, the sale is invalid, because it is a condition not necessitated by the contract, and it involves occupying the property of another, or we say it is a transaction within a transaction, because it is a hire in a sale if the benefit has a portion of the price, or a loan in a sale if it has no portion of the price. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited a transaction within a transaction. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Book of Sales, Chapter on Buildings and Keys Included in Sale, vol. 4, p. 12) al-Hidayah, Book of Sales, vol. 3, p. 28.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents the second principle: 'Inability to deliver the sold item invalidates the sale.' The author explains that if the seller cannot physically hand over the sold item, the sale becomes fasid. The text mainly reiterates the earlier example of buying fruit with a condition to leave it on the tree, but now focuses on the impossibility of delivery due to the condition. The quotes from Bada'i' al-Sana'i' and Tabyin al-Haqa'iq emphasize that such conditions lead to a prohibited double transaction (safqa fi safqa). The Hanafi position is that the sale is invalid by consensus because the condition contradicts the contract and prevents delivery.

Key Terms
تَعَدر تَسليم المبيع (ta'addur taslim al-mabee'): The inability or difficulty of the seller to deliver the sold item to the buyer.
إجارة في بيع (ijarah fi bay'): A hire contract combined with a sale, which is prohibited as a double transaction.
إعارة في بيع (i'arah fi bay'): A loan contract combined with a sale, also prohibited as a double transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second principle, what invalidates a sale?
A) The buyer's refusal to pay.
B) The seller's inability to deliver the sold item.
C) The presence of a defect in the item.
D) The lack of witnesses.

Key Takeaway
A sale is invalid if the seller cannot physically deliver the sold item due to a condition that prevents delivery, because it leads to a prohibited double transaction.

The Principle of Exclusion (Istithnā') in Sales
States a principle of exclusion in sales with examples and references

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that an item can be excluded from a sale if it can be sold alone, and apply it to scenarios involving fruits and new growth before possession.

Core Idea
Excluding a part from a sale is valid only if that part can be sold independently.

The Hanafi school allows a seller to exclude a specific part of the subject matter from a sale, provided that part is measurable and saleable on its own. This principle ensures clarity and avoids uncertainty (gharar). In this lesson, we examine the rule from Al-Hidayah and its application when new fruits appear before delivery, which can render the sale void due to impossibility of discrimination.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Identify the core rule: anything that can be sold alone can be excluded from a sale contract.
This is the foundational maxim derived from Al-Hidayah.
2
Analyze the Example
Consider the example: selling only a few known raṭls of fruit from a garden. Why is this valid? Because raṭls are measurable and individually saleable.
The excluded portion must be known by weight or count.
3
Consider the Condition of Possession
If new fruits appear before the buyer takes possession and they cannot be distinguished from the sold fruits, the sale becomes void due to ta'addhur al-tamyīz (impossibility of discrimination).
This shows that the principle has limits: when mixing makes delivery impossible, the sale fails.
4
Understand the Rationale
The invalidity arises from uncertainty (gharar) in identifying the sold item. The court requires a clear subject matter.
This rationale is key to applying the principle consistently.
5
Apply the Principle to Similar Cases
Test the rule with other items like livestock or land. Can a specific number of cattle be excluded from a large herd? Yes, if each animal is distinguishable.
The principle is broad but requires the excluded item to be independently saleable.

(۱۱) إِنَّ كُلَّ مَا يَحُوُزُ إِبْرَادُ الْعَقْدِ بِالْفِرَادِهِ يَجُوزُ اِسْتِثْنَاؤُهُ مِنَ الْعَقْدِ. ) ترجمہ: ہر وہ چیز جس کا تنہا فر وخت کرنا جائز ہو تو عقد سے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کو انفرادی اور الگ کر کے فروخت کرنا جائز ہوتو اس کو عقد بیع سے مستی کرنا بھی جائز ہے،مثلاً درخت کے پھل وغیرہ۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر بائع باغ کے پھلوں میں سے صرف چند معلوم رطل کی بیع کرے تو درست ہے، تو اسی طرح چندار طال کا استثناء بھی، وَلَوْ اشْتَرَاهَا مُطْلَقًا فَأَثْمَرَتْ ثَمَرًا آخَرَ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ فَسَدَ الْبَيْعُ لِتَعَذَّرِ التَّمْيِيزِ . (البحر الرائق: كتاب البيع، ج ۵ ص ۳۳۵) ولو اشترى الثمار مطلقا عن القطع والترك على النخيل وتركها وأثمرت مدة الترك ثمرة أخرى فإن كان قبل القبض: يعني قبل تخلية البائع بين المشترى والثمار فسد البيع لأنه لا يمكن تسليم المبيع لتعذر التمييز. (العناية: كتاب البيوع، فصل من باع دارا دخل بناؤها في البيع، ح۶ ص ٢٩٠)
الهداية: كتاب البيوع، ج ۳ ص ۲۸
(11) Everything that may be singled out in the contract alone, its exclusion from the contract is permissible. Translation: Whatever thing can be sold alone, its exclusion from the contract is also permissible. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that a thing which can be sold individually and separately, its exclusion from the contract of sale is also permissible, for example fruits of trees etc. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if the seller sells only a few known raṭls of the garden's fruits, it is valid, similarly the exclusion of a few raṭls is also valid. And if one purchases them absolutely and then before possession another fruit appears, the sale becomes void due to impossibility of discrimination. (Al-Bahr al-Raiq: Book of Sales, vol.5 p.335) And if one purchases fruits absolutely without condition of cutting or leaving on the palm trees, and leaves them, and during the leave another fruit appears, if it is before possession, i.e., before the seller gives the buyer access to the fruits, the sale becomes void because delivery of the sold item is impossible due to difficulty of discrimination. (Al-'Inayah: Book of Sales, chapter on selling a house includes its structure, vol.6 p.290) Al-Hidayah: Book of Sales, vol.3 p.28
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage introduces a key Hanafi rule regarding exceptions in sale contracts: if an item can be sold independently, then it can also be excluded from a larger sale. The author illustrates this with an example from Al-Hidayah: a seller may sell only a specific known quantity (e.g., a few raṭls) of fruits from a garden, and similarly, he may exclude that quantity from a broader sale. The passage also references two other Hanafi works (Al-Bahr al-Raiq and Al-'Inayah) to reiterate the point that if fruits are sold absolutely without specifying cutting or leaving, and new fruits grow before delivery, the sale is invalid due to difficulty in distinguishing the sold item from the new growth. This principle ensures clarity and avoids gharar (uncertainty).

Key Terms
اسْتِثْنَاء (istithnā'): A legal stipulation that excludes a specific part of the subject matter from the contract.
تَعَذُّرُ التَّمْيِيزِ (ta'addhur al-tamyīz): The impossibility of distinguishing between different items, leading to invalidity of the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It must be part of the same genus as the sold item.
B) It must be something that can be sold on its own.
C) It must be larger in quantity than the sold item.
D) It must be explicitly weighed or measured.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits exclusion of a specific part from a sale if that part is independently saleable, but such sales become void if new growth appears before possession and makes discrimination impossible.

Principle of Istithna: Exception from Sale
Explaining a Hanafi principle on exception in sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of istithna and apply it to determine whether an exception from a sale is valid.

Core Idea
What can be sold alone can be excepted; what cannot be sold alone cannot be excepted.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational Hanafi principle governing exceptions (istithna) in sale contracts. The rule is elegantly simple: if an item can be sold independently, it can also be excepted from a larger sale; if it cannot be sold alone, neither can it be excepted. The author of al-Hidayah uses this principle to resolve cases where delivery of the sold item becomes impossible due to indistinguishability, such as when new fruits appear on trees before possession. By mastering this rule, you will be able to evaluate the validity of exceptions in various sale scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making an exception (istithna) from a sale. The ruling is that it is permissible (jā'iz) under a certain condition.
2
Locate the principle
The key principle from the text: 'كل ما يجوز إيراد العقد عليه بفرادته يجوز استثناؤه من العقد' – whatever can be contracted upon individually, its exception from the contract is permissible.
3
Apply the condition
The condition is that the excepted item must be capable of being sold individually (identifiable and deliverable as a standalone item).
4
Test with positive examples
Selling a specific quantity of fruit from a garden is valid, so excepting that quantity is valid. Selling a specific sheep from a flock is valid, so excepting that sheep is valid.
Specificity is key – the item must be precisely identified.
5
Test with negative examples
Selling an unspecified sheep from a flock is invalid, so excepting an unspecified sheep is invalid. Selling a fetus or a limb of an animal alone is invalid, so excepting them is invalid.
The same logic applies in reverse.

تعذر ہو تو بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی، مثلاً بیع کے ساتھ کسی شے کا اتصال ہو گیا اور تمیز مشکل ہو صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر مشتری نے درختوں پر پھلوں کو کاٹنے اور چھوڑنے کی شرط کے بغیر مطلقاً پھل خرید لئے اور پھر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے ان درختوں میں نئے پھل بھی آگئے تو بیع فاسد ہوگی، کیونکہ مذکورہ صورت میں جب درخت پر نئے پھل بھی آگئے تو جو پھل میچ تھے ان میں امتیاز کرنا مشکل ہے اور عدم تمیز کی وجہ سے صبح حوالہ کرنا متعذر ہے اور جب مبیع کا حوالہ کرنا متعذر ہو تو بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے، لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں بھی بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔

(۱۱) إِنَّ كُلَّ مَا يَحُوُزُ إِبْرَادُ الْعَقْدِ بِالْفِرَادِهِ يَجُوزُ اِسْتِثْنَاؤُهُ مِنَ الْعَقْدِ. ) ترجمہ: ہر وہ چیز جس کا تنہا فر وخت کرنا جائز ہو تو عقد سے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کو انفرادی اور الگ کر کے فروخت کرنا جائز ہوتو اس کو عقد بیع سے مستی کرنا بھی جائز ہے،مثلاً درخت کے پھل وغیرہ۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر بائع باغ کے پھلوں میں سے صرف چند معلوم رطل کی بیع کرے تو درست ہے، تو اسی طرح چندار طال کا استثناء بھی، وَلَوْ اشْتَرَاهَا مُطْلَقًا فَأَثْمَرَتْ ثَمَرًا آخَرَ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ فَسَدَ الْبَيْعُ لِتَعَذَّرِ التَّمْيِيزِ . (البحر الرائق: كتاب البيع، ج ۵ ص ۳۳۵) ولو اشترى الثمار مطلقا عن القطع والترك على النخيل وتركها وأثمرت مدة الترك ثمرة أخرى فإن كان قبل القبض: يعني قبل تخلية البائع بين المشترى والثمار فسد البيع لأنه لا يمكن تسليم المبيع لتعذر التمييز. (العناية: كتاب البيوع، فصل من باع دارا دخل بناؤها في البيع، ح۶ ص ٢٩٠)

جس طرح غلے کے ڈھیر میں سے ایک قفیز کی بیع درست ہے، اسی طرح اس کا استثناء بھی درست ہے، جس طرح بکریوں کے ریوڑ میں سے ایک متعینہ بکری کی بیع درست ہے، اسی طرح اس کا استثناء بھی درست ہے، اور اگر وہ بکری متعینہ نہ ہو تو اس کی بیع درست نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اس کا استثناء بھی درست نہیں ہے، البتہ جن چیزوں کو انفرادی طور پر فروخت کرنا درست نہیں ہے تو ان کا استثناء بھی درست نہیں ہے، جیسے جانور کے حمل کی تنہا بیع درست نہیں ہے تو اس کا استثناء بھی درست نہیں ہے، یعنی اگر کوئی شخص صرف حمل کو فروخت کرے تو اس کی بیع درست نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر کوئی بکری کو فروخت کر کے حمل کا استثناء کرے تو وہ بھی درست نہیں ہے۔ 0
......
وَلَانَّ كُلَّ مَا جَازَ إِيرَادُ الْعَقْدِ عَلَيْهِ بِالْفِرَادِهِ جَازَ اسْتِثْنَاؤُهُ مِنْ الْعَقْدِ وَمَا لَا فَلَا وَبَيْعُ أَرْطَالٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ مِنْ الشِّمَارِ جَائِزٌ فَكَذَا اسْتِثْنَاؤُهَا، وَنَظِيرُهُ بَيْعُ شَاةٍ مُعَيَّنَةٍ مِنْ الْقَطِيعِ فَإِنَّهُ يَجُوزُ فَكَذَا اسْتِثْنَاؤُهَا وَلَوْ كَانَتْ مَجْهُولَةٌ بِأَنْ بَاعَ شَاةً مِنْهَا بِغَيْرِ عَيْنِهَا لَا يَجُوزُ فَكَذَا اسْتِتْنَاؤُهَا وَعَلَى هَذَا أَطْرَافُ الْحَيَوَانِ. (تبيين الحقائق: كتاب البيوع، ج۴ ص ۱۳)
ولهذا قال: ينبغي أن يجوز لأن الأصل أن ما يجوز إيراد العقد عليه بانفراده يجوز استثناؤه من العقد وبيع قفيز من صبرة جائز، فكذا استثناؤه) وينعكس إلى أن ما لا يجوز إيراد العقد عليه بانفراده لا يجوز استثناؤه (بخلاف استثناء الحمل وأطراف الحيوان، لأنه لا يجوز بيعه فكذا استثناؤه) صورة استثنائه الحمل أن يقول: بعتك هذه الشاة إلا حملها، وصورة استثناء أطراف الحيوان بأن يقول: بعتك هذه الشاة إلا جلدها أو غيره، فإنه لا يجوز لا في حضر ولا في سفر البناية: كتاب البيوع، فصل في بيان ما يدخل تحت البيع من غير ذکره، ج۸ ص ۴۲)
The principle from Hidayah: When delivery becomes impossible, the sale becomes invalid. For example, if something becomes attached to the sale item and distinguishing it becomes difficult. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if the buyer purchased fruits on trees without stipulating cutting or leaving, and before taking possession new fruits appear, the sale becomes invalid because distinguishing the original fruits from the new ones is difficult, and delivery becomes impossible. When delivery is impossible, the sale becomes invalid. (11) Ruling: 'Indeed, everything that can be the subject of a contract individually, its exception from the contract is permissible.' Translation: Every item that can be sold individually, its exception (istithna) from the contract is also permissible. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that an item that can be sold separately may also be excepted from the sale contract, such as fruits on trees. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if the seller sells only a known number of ratls from the garden fruits, it is valid, and similarly, excepting that number is valid. As in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 'And if he buys them absolutely, and they produce another fruit before possession, the sale becomes invalid due to the impossibility of distinguishing.' And in al-'Inayah: 'And if he buys the fruits absolutely without stipulating cutting or leaving on the palm trees, and leaves them, and they produce another fruit during the period of leaving, then if it is before possession—meaning before the seller leaves the buyer and the fruits—the sale becomes invalid because it is impossible to deliver the sold item due to the impossibility of distinguishing.' And in al-Hidayah: (source omitted). On page 37: Just as selling one qafiz from a heap of grain is valid, so is excepting it valid. Just as selling a specific sheep from a flock is valid, so is excepting it valid. And if the sheep is not specified, its sale is not valid, and similarly its exception is not valid. However, items that cannot be sold individually—their exception is also not valid. For example, selling the fetus of an animal alone is not valid, so excepting it is not valid. That is, if a person sells only the fetus, the sale is not valid; similarly, if a person sells a sheep and excepts the fetus, that is also not valid. The Arabic texts from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and al-Binayah further elaborate the principle: 'And because everything that can be the subject of a contract individually, its exception from the contract is permissible, and what cannot, is not. And selling known ratls from fruits is permissible, so is excepting them. Its analogy is selling a specific sheep from the flock; it is permissible, so is excepting it. And if it is unknown, by selling a sheep from it without specification, it is not permissible, and similarly its exception. And on this are the limbs of animals.' And in al-Binayah: 'Therefore, he said: It should be permissible because the principle is that whatever can be the subject of a contract individually, its exception from the contract is permissible, and selling a qafiz from a pile is permissible, so is its exception. And the converse applies: whatever cannot be the subject of a contract individually, its exception is not permissible, contrary to excepting the fetus and limbs of an animal, because selling them is not permissible, so is their exception. The form of excepting the fetus: he says, "I sold you this sheep except its fetus." And the form of excepting limbs of an animal: he says, "I sold you this sheep except its skin or other part." It is not permissible, neither in residence nor in travel.'
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage presents a key Hanafi principle regarding exception (istithna) in sale contracts. The rule is: anything that can validly be sold individually can also be excepted from a sale. Conversely, if something cannot be sold alone, it cannot be excepted. The author first applies this to a scenario where fruits are bought, and new fruits appear before possession – the sale becomes invalid because the original and new fruits cannot be distinguished, making delivery impossible. Then the principle is stated in Arabic: 'Every thing that can be the subject of a contract individually, its exception from the contract is permissible.' This is followed by examples: selling a specific quantity of fruit from a garden, selling a specific sheep from a flock (permissible, so exception is permissible), but selling an unspecified sheep or the fetus of an animal (not permissible individually, so exception is also not permissible). The passage cites several authoritative Hanafi texts – al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-'Inayah, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and al-Binayah – to support and expand on the rule. The overall message is clear: the validity of an exception is directly tied to the validity of selling that item independently.

Key Terms
إِبْرَادُ الْعَقْدِ (īrād al-'aqd): The act of making a contract (on a specific item).
بِالْفِرَادِهِ (bil-firādi): Individually, separately, as a standalone item.
اسْتِثْنَاء (istithnā'): Exception, exclusion from a contract (e.g., I sell you the herd except this sheep).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following exceptions is valid according to the Hanafi principle of istithna?
A) Excepting the fetus from the sale of a cow
B) Excepting a specific sheep ('the one with the bell') from a flock
C) Excepting 'a handful of grain' from a sack without specifying amount
D) Excepting the skin of a goat from the sale of the live goat

Key Takeaway
The validity of an exception in a sale contract depends on whether the excepted item can be sold individually; if it cannot, the exception is invalid.

6 min
The Principle of Exception (Istithna) in Sales
Explains the rule linking exception validity to salability of the item alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on istithna and apply it to determine the validity of an exception clause in a sale contract.

Core Idea
In Hanafi sales law, anything that can be sold alone can be excepted; what cannot be sold alone cannot be excepted.

When selling a larger item or bundle, parties sometimes wish to exclude a part of it from the sale. This clause is called istithna (exception). The Hanafi school establishes a clear principle: the validity of an exception depends on whether that part can be sold individually. This lesson unpacks that rule through classical examples from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and al-Binaya, showing how qiyas (analogy) grounds the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is including an istithna clause in a sale contract. The ruling is conditional: valid (sahih) if the excepted item can be sold independently, otherwise invalid (batil).
This is a ruling on the validity of a contract term.
2
Recognize the governing principle
The principle: 'Everything that is permissible to contract upon individually is permissible to except from a contract, and what is not, then not.' This is the core legal maxim.
The principle is derived from qiyas on the general permissibility of selling individual items.
3
Apply the principle to examples
Work through the examples: a qafiz from a grain heap (valid), a specified goat from a flock (valid), an unspecified goat (invalid), the fetus or limbs of an animal (invalid).
Focus on the condition of specifiability and independent salability.
4
Examine the converse
The rule works both ways: if an item cannot be sold alone, it cannot be excepted. This prevents uncertainty (gharar) in contracts.
The converse is explicitly stated: 'what is not permissible to contract upon individually, its exception is not permissible.'
5
Note the proof structure
The proof is qiyas jali (clear analogy). The asl (original case) is the sale of an individual item (e.g., one qafiz from a heap), which is valid. The far' (new case) is the exception of that item from a larger sale. The illa (effective cause) is the ability to contract upon it individually.
This demonstrates how Hanafi fiqh uses analogical reasoning to derive contract rules.
