Istihqaq does not prevent the completion of the transaction. Translation: Istihqaq does not prevent the completion of the contract. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if a claimant for part of the sold item emerges, it does not affect the contract; he will not have the option to return it provided that division does not cause harm. The author of Hidayah, mentioning this principle, is stating that if a person sold wheat, then a claimant for part of it emerged, the buyer does not have the option to return the good wheat, because in this case a claimant for part of the seed emerged, and because of the claim on part of the sold item, the contract remains in effect for the remainder, because after possession of a measurable or weighable item, the claim does not prevent the completion of the contract; rather, the buyer will take back from the seller the price commensurate with the claimed part, because in measurable or weighable items division is not a defect. Unlike cloth, where in the case of a claim there will be an option to return, because cutting and dividing cloth is a defect. And if a claimant for some part of the item emerges, and the buyer finds a defect in it, and the seller wants to allocate the price on the assumption of return, and the seller says 'I sold you this and another with it' and the buyer says 'You sold me only it', then the word is the buyer's, because the dispute is over the amount received and the word is that of the receiver, because he knows best what he received, as in the case of usurpation: if the usurper and the person from whom something was usurped dispute, and the latter says 'You usurped two slaves from me' and the usurper says 'One slave', the word is the usurper's because he is the receiver. (Al-Inayah: Book of Sales, Chapter of Option of Defect, vol. 6, pp. 385-386) Al-Hidayah: Book of Sales, Chapter of Option of Defect, vol. 3, p. 48.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim (qāʿidah) from the Hanafi school: that a claim of ownership (istihqāq) by a third party over part of a sold item does not invalidate the entire sale. The passage type is a ruling with explanatory commentary drawn from authoritative Hanafi sources like Al-Hidayah and Al-Inayah. The principle is that in measurable (makīl) or weighable (mawzūn) items, such as wheat, the contract remains valid for the remainder even after part is claimed; the buyer cannot return the remaining portion but instead recovers a proportional part of the price. This is because dividing such items does not constitute a defect. In contrast, for items like cloth, which are damaged by cutting, the buyer has the option to return the entire piece if part is claimed. The passage also addresses a related dispute over the quantity received, where the receiver's word is taken, analogous to the law of usurpation (ghaṣb). A narration from Abu Hanifa suggests an option to return to avoid the burden of division, but the apparent position (ẓāhir al-riwāyah) is that there is no such option for measurable/weighable goods.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqāq): A third-party claim of ownership over part of the sold item.
مبيع (mabīʿ): The item sold in a sales contract.
كيلي (makīl): Items sold by volume measure (e.g., wheat, barley).
موزون (mawzūn): Items sold by weight (e.g., rice, dates).
ثوب (thawb): Cloth or fabric.
عيي (ʿayb): A defect that gives the buyer an option of return (khiyār al-ʿayb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The buyer can return the entire item.
B) The buyer can return only the claimed portion.
C) The buyer cannot return the remaining item and must pay the full price.
D) The buyer must accept the remaining item and get a price reduction for the claimed portion.

Key Takeaway
A third-party claim on part of a makīl/mawzūn sold item does not void the sale; the buyer gets a price reduction, while for cloth he has an option to return.

The Maxim: Sale of What Cannot Be Delivered is Invalid
Maxim with illustrative istihqāq case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim regarding the invalidity of selling what cannot be delivered and apply it to distinguish between measurable/weighable items and other items when part of the sold item is reclaimed (istihqāq).

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if the seller cannot deliver; for measurable goods, partial reclamation does not create a right to return.

This lesson presents a foundational maxim of Hanafi sales law: the sale of an item that the seller cannot physically deliver is not permissible. The passage from Al-Hidayah states the maxim and then applies it to a scenario where a portion of the sold item is reclaimed by a third party. The commentary clarifies the different treatment of measurable/weighable goods versus other types of goods, and notes a slight difference within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Identify the exact wording of the maxim as given in the source: 'Bay'u mā huwa ghayru maqdūr al-taslīm lā yajūz'.
This forms the core ruling.
2
Understand the condition of delivery
Recognize that the key condition is the seller's ability (qudra) to deliver the item at the time of the contract. Items that are physically absent, lost, or only potentially accessible fall under this prohibition.
The maxim is not restricted to physical possession but includes legal or practical ability.
3
Apply to the istihqāq scenario
Consider the case where a third party reclaims part of the sold item after the sale. The source distinguishes between measurable/weighable items (makīl/mawzūn) and other items (e.g., cloth, slaves). For the former, the buyer has no option to return the remaining part because division is not a defect; for the latter, division is a defect and the buyer may return.
This illustrates how the general maxim interacts with specific categories of goods.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf
A narration from Abu Hanifa allows the buyer to return the remaining part to avoid the burden of division, but the apparent (ẓāhir) position in the school denies this option. Note the basis: for measurable goods, division does not affect value or utility.
The ẓāhir al-riwāyah is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب البيع الفاسد
(۲۱) بَيْعُ مَا هُوَ غَيْرُ مَقْدُورِ التَّسْلِيم لَا يَجُوزُ . )
ترجمہ: ایسی شے کا فروخت کرنا جس کے حوالہ کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو جائز نہیں ہے۔ وَلَوْ اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُهُ لَمْ يُخَيَّرُ فِي رَدْ مَا بَقِيَ وَلَوْ ثَوْبًا خُيِّرَ) يَعْنِي لَوْ اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُ الْمَكِيلِ أَوْ الْمَوزُونِ لَمُ يُخَيَّرُ فِي رَدَّ الْبَاقِي، وَلَوْ اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُ الثَّوبِ خُيْرَ فِي رَدْ مَا بَقِيَ، لأنَّ الشَّرِكَةَ فِي الْمَكِيلِ وَالْمَوْزُونَ لَا تَعُدُّ عَيْبًا، لأنَّ التَّبْعِيضَ لَا يَضُرُّهُمَا وَالاسْتِحْقَاقُ لَا يَمْنَعُ تَمَامَ الصَّفَقَةِ، لِأَنَّ الْعَقْدَ حَقُّ الْعَاقِدِ وَتَمَامُهُ بِرِضًا الْعَاقِدِ لَا بِرِضًا الْمَالِكِ بِخِلَافِ الثَّوْبِ حَيْثُ يَثْبُتُ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ فِيمَا إِذَا اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُهُ، لأَنَّ التَّشْقِيصَ فِيهِ عَيْبٌ وَقَدْ كَانَ وَقْتُ الْبَيْعِ فَيَرُدُّهُ. (تبيين الحقائق: كتاب البيوع، باب خيار العيب، ج۴ ص ۴۱) (قَوْلُهُ وَلَوْ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَهُ) أَى بَعْضَ الْمَكِيلِ أَوِ الْمَوْزُونِ فَلَا خِيَارَ لِلْمُشْتَرِى فِي رَدْ مَا بَقِيَ بَلْ يَلْزَمُهُ أَنْ لَا يَرُدَّهُ، وَرُوِيَ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ لَهُ رَدُّهُ دَفْعًا لِضَرَرٍ مُؤْنَةِ الْقِسْمَةِ (وَجُهُ الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّهُ لَا يَضُرُّهُ التَّبْعِيضُ لَا فِي الْقِيمَةِ وَلَا فِي الْمَنْفَعَةِ، أَمَّا فِي الْقِيمَةِ فَإِنَّ الْمُدَّ مِنَ الْقَمُحِ يُبَاعُ عَلَى وِزَانِ مَا يُبَاعُ بِهِ الْإِرْدَبُّ وَالْغِرَارَةُ، وَأَمَّا فِي الْمَنْفَعَةِ فَظَاهِرٌ فَلَا يَتَضَرَّرُ بِهِ، بِخِلَافِ غَيْرِهِ فَإِنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا يُفْصَلُ يَصِيرُ مَعِيبًا بِتَبْعِيضِهِ فَإِنَّ الْفَضْلَةَ مِنْ الثَّوْبِ كَالذَّرَاعِ إِذَا نُودِيَ عَلَيْهِ فِي السُّوقِ لَا تَبْلُغُ قِيمَتُهُ مُتَّصِلا بِبَاقِي الثَّوْبِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا لَا يُفْصَلُ كَالْعَبْدِ يَصِيرُ مَعِيبًا بِعَيْبِ الشَّرِكَةِ، بِخِلَافِ الْمَكِيلٍ لَا يَتَعَيَّبُ بِالشَّرِكَةِ. فتح القدير: كتاب البيوع، باب خيار
العيب، ج ۶ ص ۳۸۹
الهداية: كتاب البيوع، باب البيع الفاسد، ج ۳ ص ۵۲، ۵۳
Chapter of Invalid Sale. (21) Sale of what is not capable of delivery is not permissible. Translation: Selling an item that one is not able to deliver is not permissible. And if part of it is claimed, he is not given an option to return what remains; but if it is cloth, he is given an option. Meaning: if part of a measurable or weighable item is claimed, he is not given an option to return the remainder; if part of a cloth is claimed, he is given an option to return what remains, because partnership in measurable and weighable items is not considered a defect, since division does not harm them, and the claim does not prevent completion of the transaction, because the contract is the right of the contracting parties and its completion is by their consent, not by the consent of the owner. Unlike cloth, where he has an option when part is claimed, because division in it is a defect, and it existed at the time of sale, so he returns it. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Book of Sales, Chapter of Option of Defect, vol. 4, p. 41) (His saying: 'and if part of it is claimed' means part of a measurable or weighable item, so the buyer has no option to return what remains, rather he must not return it. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he may return it to avoid the harm of the burden of division. The apparent position is that division does not harm him, neither in value nor in benefit. As for value, a mudd of wheat is sold at the same rate as an irdabb or a ghirarah. As for benefit, it is obvious that he is not harmed by it. Unlike other items: if it is something that can be separated, it becomes defective by division; for example, a remnant of cloth like a cubit, when auctioned in the market, its value does not reach its value when attached to the rest of the cloth. And if it is something that cannot be separated, like a slave, it becomes defective by the defect of partnership, unlike measurable items which do not become defective by partnership. (Fath al-Qadir: Book of Sales, Chapter of Option of Defect, vol. 6, p. 389) Al-Hidayah: Book of Sales, Chapter of Invalid Sale, vol. 3, pp. 52-53.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents a second legal maxim: the sale of something that the seller cannot physically deliver is not permissible (lā yajūz). The passage type is a ruling statement followed by supporting commentary from Hanafi sources. The author then repeats the ruling from the previous maxim about istihqāq, applying it here as an example or reinforcement. The commentary from Tabyin al-Haqāʾiq and Fatḥ al-Qadīr explains the reasoning: for measurable/weighable items, the buyer cannot return the remaining part if part is claimed because division is not a defect; for cloth or indivisible items like a slave, it is a defect. A narration from Abu Hanifa allows return to avoid the burden of division, but the apparent (ẓāhir) position is that there is no such option. The maxim itself is fundamental to Hanafi sales law and is cited from Al-Hidayah's chapter on invalid sales.

Key Terms
بيع ما هو غير مقدور التسليم (bayʿu mā huwa ghayru maqdūr al-taslīm): Sale of an item that the seller cannot physically hand over to the buyer (e.g., a runaway animal, a lost item).
بيع فاسد (bayʿ fāsid): An invalid sale that is defective in one of its conditions but can be rectified in some cases.
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery of the sold item to the buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The sale of an item the seller cannot deliver is invalid (fāsid) in the Hanafi school; for measurable/weighable goods, partial reclamation does not create a right to return the remainder.

6 min
Invalidity of Sale When Delivery Is Impossible
Explains the principle of invalid sale due to non-deliverability with applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of deliverability to determine the validity of a sale and explain the ruling on partial reclamation of makil/mawzun items.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if the seller cannot deliver; partial reclamation of measured/weighed items gives no option to return.

This lesson introduces a fundamental condition for the validity of a sale in Hanafi fiqh: the seller must be able to deliver the sold item. The passage establishes this principle and then applies it to two scenarios: when a third party reclaims part of a measured or weighed item, and when the item is a fish or bird that cannot be easily retrieved. Understanding these applications helps you evaluate real-world sale contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Identify the core ruling: the sale of something not deliverable is invalid. This is a condition for validity.
The Arabic phrase is 'بيع ما هو غير مقدور التسليم لا يجوز'.
2
Identify the conditions for validity
The seller must own the item and be able to deliver it. Inability to deliver (due to lack of ownership or physical impossibility) renders the sale batil.
These are shurut (conditions) for a valid sale.
3
Apply to partial reclamation of makil/mawzun
If part of a measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun) item is reclaimed by a third party, the buyer has no option to return the remainder. This is because dividing such items does not harm their value or utility.
Co-ownership is not considered a defect in these items.
4
Distinguish cloth and indivisible items
For a cloth (thawb) or a slave, splitting creates a defect, so the buyer has the option to return the remainder if part is reclaimed. This contrasts with makil/mawzun.
The defect (ʿayb) is the division itself or co-ownership.
5
Apply to fish and birds
Selling fish in water before catching is invalid due to non-ownership. Selling a bird that has been released and cannot be easily retrieved is also invalid due to inability to deliver.
There is a minor intra-Hanafi difference regarding fish released into a pond that can be retrieved easily.

باب البيع الفاسد
(۲۱) بَيْعُ مَا هُوَ غَيْرُ مَقْدُورِ التَّسْلِيم لَا يَجُوزُ . )
ترجمہ: ایسی شے کا فروخت کرنا جس کے حوالہ کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو جائز نہیں ہے۔ وَلَوْ اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُهُ لَمْ يُخَيَّرُ فِي رَدْ مَا بَقِيَ وَلَوْ ثَوْبًا خُيِّرَ) يَعْنِي لَوْ اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُ الْمَكِيلِ أَوْ الْمَوزُونِ لَمُ يُخَيَّرُ فِي رَدَّ الْبَاقِي، وَلَوْ اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُ الثَّوبِ خُيْرَ فِي رَدْ مَا بَقِيَ، لأنَّ الشَّرِكَةَ فِي الْمَكِيلِ وَالْمَوْزُونَ لَا تُعَدُّ عَيْبًا، لأنَّ التَّبْعِيضَ لَا يَضُرُّهُمَا وَالاسْتِحْقَاقُ لَا يَمْنَعُ تَمَامَ الصَّفَقَةِ، لِأَنَّ الْعَقْدَ حَقُّ الْعَاقِدِ وَتَمَامُهُ بِرِضًا الْعَاقِدِ لَا بِرِضًا الْمَالِكِ بِخِلَافِ الثَّوْبِ حَيْثُ يَثْبُتُ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ فِيمَا إِذَا اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُهُ، لأَنَّ التَّشْقِيصَ فِيهِ عَيْبٌ وَقَدْ كَانَ وَقْتُ الْبَيْعِ فَيَرُدُّهُ. (تبيين الحقائق: كتاب البيوع، باب خيار العيب، ج۴ ص ۴۱) (قَوْلُهُ وَلَوْ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَهُ) أَى بَعْضَ الْمَكِيلِ أَوِ الْمَوْزُونِ فَلَا خِيَارَ لِلْمُشْتَرِى فِي رَدْ مَا بَقِيَ بَلْ يَلْزَمُهُ أَنْ لَا يَرُدَّهُ، وَرُوِيَ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ لَهُ رَدُّهُ دَفْعًا لِضَرَرٍ مُؤْنَةِ الْقِسْمَةِ (وَجُهُ الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّهُ لَا يَضُرُّهُ التَّبْعِيضُ لَا فِي الْقِيمَةِ وَلَا فِي الْمَنْفَعَةِ، أَمَّا فِي الْقِيمَةِ فَإِنَّ الْمُدَّ مِنَ الْقَمُحِ يُبَاعُ عَلَى وِزَانِ مَا يُبَاعُ بِهِ الْإِرْدَبُّ وَالْغِرَارَةُ، وَأَمَّا فِي الْمَنْفَعَةِ فَظَاهِرٌ فَلَا يَتَضَرَّرُ بِهِ، بِخِلَافِ غَيْرِهِ فَإِنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا يُفْصَلُ يَصِيرُ مَعِيبًا بِتَبْعِيضِهِ فَإِنَّ الْفَضْلَةَ مِنْ الثَّوْبِ كَالذَّرَاعِ إِذَا نُودِيَ عَلَيْهِ فِي السُّوقِ لَا تَبْلُغُ قِيمَتُهُ مُتَّصِلا بِبَاقِي الثَّوْبِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا لَا يُفْصَلُ كَالْعَبْدِ يَصِيرُ مَعِيبًا بِعَيْبِ الشَّرِكَةِ، بِخِلَافِ الْمَكِيلٍ لَا يَتَعَيَّبُ بِالشَّرِكَةِ. فتح القدير: كتاب البيوع، باب خيار العيب، ج ۶ ص ۳۸۹
الهداية: كتاب البيوع، باب البيع الفاسد، ج ۳ ص ۵۲، ۵۳
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایسی چیز کو فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے جس
کے حوالہ کرنے پر بائع قادر نہ ہو ۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ شکار کرنے سے پہلے مچھلی کو فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ شکار سے پہلے وہ اس کا مالک نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر شکار کر کے ایسے بڑے تالاب میں چھوڑ دیا کہ بغیر حیلے کے اس کا پکڑنا مشکل ہو تو بھی بیع جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس کے حوالے کرنے پر بائع قادر نہیں ہے، اور ہر ایسی چیز کو فروخت کرنا جس کے حوالہ کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو تو بیع جائز نہیں ہے، تو بیع کے جواز کے لیے شرط یہ ہے کہ بائع اس شے کا مالک ہو اور اُس کے حوالہ کرنے پر قادر ہو۔ اسی طرح اگر پرندہ ہوا میں اُڑ رہا ہو تو اس کی بیع درست نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ وہ غیر مملوک ہے، اور اگر کسی نے پرندے کو پکڑنے کے بعد اڑا دیا اور پھر فروخت کیا تو بھی بیچ درست نہیں ہے، اس لیے کہ اس صورت میں وہ اس کے سپر د کرنے پر قادر نہیں ہے۔
ولا يجوز بيع السمك فى الماء قبل أن يصطاده ولا بيع الطير في الهواء ) اعلم أنه إذا باع سمكا في حوض إن كان لم يأخذه قط لا يجوز له بيعه، لأنه باع ما لا يملك، وإن أخذه ثم أرسله جاز البيع إن كان يقدر على أخذه من غير صيد وللمشترى خيار الرؤية، وإن كان لا يمكن أخذه إلا بحيلة واصطياد لا يجوز البيع إلا إذا قدر على التسليم وهذا قول العراقيين، أما عند أهل بلخى فلا يجوز، وإن قدر على التسليم، وأما بيع الطير فى الهواء فلأنه غير مملوك قبل الأخذ، وإن أرسل من يده فغير مقدور التسليم. (الجوهرة النيرة: كتاب البيوع، باب البيع الفاسد، ج ۱ ص ۲۰۱)
ولا يجوز أى لا يصح بيع السمك فى الماء) قبل صيده، لأنه بيع ما ليس عنده، أو بعده صيده ثم ألقى فيه ولا يؤخذ منه إلا بحيلة، للعجز عن التسليم
When part (of the sold item) is reclaimed, the buyer does not have the option to return the remainder. And if it is a cloth, he has the option. Meaning, if part of a measured or weighed item is reclaimed, the buyer is not given the option to return the remainder. But if part of a cloth is reclaimed, he is given the option to return the remainder, because co-ownership in measured and weighed items is not considered a defect, since dividing them does not harm them. Reclamation does not prevent completion of the transaction, because the contract is the right of the contracting parties, and its completion is by the consent of the contracting parties, not by the consent of the owner. Unlike a cloth, where he has the option when part is reclaimed, because splitting is a defect in it, and at the time of sale it was whole, so he may return it. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab Khiyar al-‘Ayb, vol. 4 p. 41) (His statement: 'And if part of it is reclaimed' means part of the measured or weighed item, so there is no option for the buyer to return what remains; rather, it is obligatory upon him not to return it. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he may return it to avoid the burden of division. The apparent position is that division does not harm him, neither in value nor in benefit. As for value, a mudd of wheat is sold at the same rate as a irdabb or ghirara. As for benefit, it is obvious that he is not harmed by it. Unlike other items, for if it is something that can be cut like a cloth, it becomes defective by its division, for a leftover piece of cloth like a cubit, when called in the market, its value does not reach its value when attached to the rest of the cloth. And if it is something that cannot be cut like a slave, it becomes defective by the defect of co-ownership. Unlike a measured item, it does not become defective by co-ownership. (Fath al-Qadir: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab Khiyar al-‘Ayb, vol. 6 p. 389) (Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay‘ al-Fasid, vol. 3 pp. 52, 53) Commentary: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that selling an item that the seller is not able to deliver is not permissible. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the principle, explains that selling fish before catching it is not permissible, because before catching, he is not its owner. Similarly, if after catching he releases it into a large pond from which it is difficult to retrieve without a trick, the sale is also not permissible, because the seller is not able to deliver it. And every such item whose delivery the seller is not able to make, its sale is not permissible. So for the validity of a sale, the condition is that the seller owns the item and is able to deliver it. Similarly, if a bird is flying in the air, its sale is not valid because it is not owned. And if someone catches a bird then releases it and then sells it, the sale is still not valid, because in that case he is not able to deliver it. And it is not permissible to sell fish in water before catching it, nor a bird in the air. Know that if he sells fish in a basin, if he has never taken it, it is not permissible for him to sell it, because he sold what he does not own. If he took it then released it, the sale is permissible if he can take it without hunting, and the buyer has the option of inspection. If it cannot be taken except by a trick and hunting, the sale is not permissible except if he is able to deliver. This is the saying of the Iraqis. As for the people of Balkh, they do not permit it even if he is able to deliver. As for the sale of a bird in the air, it is because it is not owned before being taken, and if he releases it from his hand, it is not possible to deliver. (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay‘ al-Fasid, vol. 1 p. 201) And it is not permissible, meaning not valid, to sell fish in water before catching it, because it is selling what he does not have, or after catching it and then throwing it back where it cannot be taken except by a trick, due to inability to deliver.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with expansion from a Hanafi fiqh textbook. It opens by establishing the foundational legal principle: the sale of something that the seller is unable to deliver is invalid. The Arabic states: 'بيع ما هو غير مقدور التسليم لا يجوز' — the sale of what is not possible to deliver is not permissible. This is a well-known condition for the validity of a sale contract in the Hanafi school.

The passage then elaborates on a specific scenario: if part of the sold item is reclaimed (istihaqq) by a third party who proves ownership. For example, if someone buys a certain measure of grain, and a third party proves that part of that grain is actually his, the buyer does not have the option (khiyar) to return the remaining grain. This is because dividing a measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun) item does not harm its value or utility; a small amount of wheat is sold at the same rate per measure as a large amount. The sale contract is completed by the mutual consent of the buyer and seller, not by the consent of the reclaiming owner. However, if the item is a cloth (thawb), the buyer does have the option to return the remainder if part is reclaimed, because cutting a cloth creates a defect — a detached piece is worth less than when attached. Similarly, indivisible items like a slave become defective through co-ownership (shirkah). The text cites Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and Fath al-Qadir, noting that according to a transmission from Abu Hanifa, the buyer may return the remainder to avoid the burden of division, but the apparent position (zahir al-madhhab) holds no return.

The second part applies the same principle to fish and birds. Selling fish in water before catching is invalid because the seller does not own it. If the seller catches the fish and then releases it into a pond from which it cannot be retrieved without difficulty, the sale is also invalid due to inability to deliver. Similarly, selling a bird while flying or after release without easy recapture is invalid. The text quotes Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, which mentions a difference of opinion: the Iraqi scholars permit the sale if the seller can retrieve the fish easily, while the Balkhi scholars forbid it even then. The relied-upon position is that the sale is invalid if delivery is not possible with ease. This lesson thus emphasizes that both ownership and ability to deliver are essential conditions for a valid sale according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
بيع ما هو غير مقدور التسليم (bay‘ ma huwa ghayr maqdur al-taslim): Sale of something that the seller is not able to deliver; such a sale is invalid.
استحقاق (istihqaq): Reclamation of part or all of the sold item by a third party who proves ownership.
مكيل (makil): Items sold by volume measure (e.g., grain, wheat).
موزون (mawzun): Items sold by weight (e.g., gold, silver, oil).
خيار (khiyar): Option to rescind a contract; here, the option to return the remainder of the purchased item.
عيب (‘ayb): A defect that reduces the value or utility of an item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is selling fish in water before catching it invalid?
A) Because the fish is not yet caught.
B) Because the seller does not own the fish and cannot deliver it.
C) Because the buyer cannot see the fish.
D) Because the price cannot be determined.

Key Takeaway
A sale is valid only if the seller owns the item and can deliver it; partial reclamation of measured/weighed items does not create a defect or option to return.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Selling Fish and Birds: Ownership and Delivery
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sale of fish after release

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two essential conditions for a valid sale in Hanafi law and distinguish between the Iraqi and Balkhi positions on the sale of a recaptured fish.

Core Idea
A sale requires both ownership and ability to deliver; if the seller can recapture a fish after release, the sale is valid per Iraqi Hanafis.

This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah discusses a fundamental Hanafi principle: a sale is invalid if the seller cannot deliver the item. The author applies this to fish in water and birds in the air, but a dispute arises within the school when the seller previously captured the item and then released it. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of the condition of qadir 'ala al-taslim.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi principle
Identify the condition for a valid sale: the seller must own the item and be able to deliver it (qadir 'ala al-taslim). This is derived from the prohibition of selling what one does not possess.
This principle applies to all sales, not just fish and birds.
2
Apply to fish before capture
Selling a fish in water before catching it is invalid because the seller neither owns it nor can deliver it. The same applies to a bird in the air.
Non-owned property cannot be sold.
3
Distinguish the case of a recaptured fish
If the seller caught the fish and then released it into a tank, the ruling changes depending on whether he can recapture it without difficulty. This is where the intra-Hanafi dispute arises.
The fish is now owned, but delivery may be difficult.
4
Analyze the Iraqi position
The Iraqi scholars allow the sale if the seller can recapture the fish without trapping (i.e., easily). The buyer also has the option of inspection.
They prioritize ownership and practical ability to deliver.
5
Contrast with the Balkhi position
The Balkhi scholars prohibit the sale even if the seller can deliver, possibly due to uncertainty or the difficulty of recapture. The text reports this difference without ruling on it.
This shows that even within a school, regional differences existed.

صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ شکار کرنے سے پہلے مچھلی کو فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ شکار سے پہلے وہ اس کا مالک نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر شکار کر کے ایسے بڑے تالاب میں چھوڑ دیا کہ بغیر حیلے کے اس کا پکڑنا مشکل ہو تو بھی بیع جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس کے حوالے کرنے پر بائع قادر نہیں ہے، اور ہر ایسی چیز کو فروخت کرنا جس کے حوالہ کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو تو بیع جائز نہیں ہے، تو بیع کے جواز کے لیے شرط یہ ہے کہ بائع اس شے کا مالک ہو اور اُس کے حوالہ کرنے پر قادر ہو۔ اسی طرح اگر پرندہ ہوا میں اُڑ رہا ہو تو اس کی بیع درست نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ وہ غیر مملوک ہے، اور اگر کسی نے پرندے کو پکڑنے کے بعد اڑا دیا اور پھر فروخت کیا تو بھی بیچ درست نہیں ہے، اس لیے کہ اس صورت میں وہ اس کے سپر د کر نے پر قادر نہیں ہے۔

ولا يجوز بيع السمك فى الماء قبل أن يصطاده ولا بيع الطير في الهواء ) اعلم أنه إذا باع سمكا في حوض إن كان لم يأخذه قط لا يجوز له بيعه، لأنه باع ما لا يملك، وإن أخذه ثم أرسله جاز البيع إن كان يقدر على أخذه من غير صيد وللمشترى خيار الرؤية، وإن كان لا يمكن أخذه إلا بحيلة واصطياد لا يجوز البيع إلا إذا قدر على التسليم وهذا قول العراقيين، أما عند أهل بلخى فلا يجوز، وإن قدر على التسليم، وأما بيع الطير فى الهواء فلأنه غير مملوك قبل الأخذ، وإن أرسل من يده فغير مقدور التسليم. (الجوهرة النيرة: كتاب البيوع، باب البيع الفاسد، ج ۱ ص ۲۰۱)

ولا يجوز أى لا يصح بيع السمك فى الماء) قبل صيده، لأنه بيع ما ليس عنده، أو بعده صيده ثم ألقى فيه ولا يؤخذ منه إلا بحيلة، للعجز عن التسليم
Principles of Hidayah, Third. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that it is not permissible to sell something that the seller is not able to deliver. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, is stating that selling fish before catching it is not permissible because before catching it he is not its owner. Similarly, if after catching it he releases it into a large pond such that without a trick it is difficult to catch, then also the sale is not permissible because the seller is not able to deliver it. And selling any thing that one cannot deliver is not permissible. So the condition for permissibility of sale is that the seller be the owner of the thing and be able to deliver it. Similarly, if a bird is flying in the air, its sale is not valid because it is not owned. And if someone after catching a bird releases it and then sells it, the sale is also not valid because in that case he is not able to deliver it. And it is not permissible to sell fish in water before catching it, nor the bird in the air. Know that if one sells a fish in a tank, if he has never caught it, its sale is not permissible because he sells what he does not own. And if he catches it and then releases it, the sale is permissible if he can catch it without trapping, and the buyer has the option of inspection. But if it cannot be caught except by a trick and trapping, the sale is not permissible unless he is able to deliver. This is the saying of the Iraqis. As for the people of Balkh, they say it is not permissible even if he can deliver. As for selling the bird in the air, it is because it is not owned before taking, and if released from the hand, it is not deliverable. (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah). And it is not permissible, i.e., the sale of fish in water before catching it, because it is selling what one does not have, or after catching it then throwing it in such that it cannot be taken except by a trick, due to inability to deliver.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of fish in water and birds in air. The core ruling is that such sales are invalid if the seller neither owns nor can deliver the item. The commentator explains the conditions: if the seller has never caught the fish, it is a sale of non-owned property. If he catches and releases it, the sale is permissible only if he can recapture it without difficulty; otherwise it is invalid. The Iraqi jurists (عند العراقيين) allow the sale if the seller can deliver, while the Balkhi jurists (عند أهل بلخى) prohibit it absolutely even if delivery is possible. For birds in the air, the sale is invalid because the bird is not owned before capture, and if released from the hand, delivery is impossible. This highlights the Hanafi principle that ability to deliver (القدرة على التسليم) is a condition for valid sale, and ownership is also required.

Key Terms
قادر على التسليم (qadir 'ala al-taslim): Ability to deliver the sold item to the buyer, a condition for the validity of sale in Hanafi law.
بيع ما ليس عنده (bay' ma laysa 'indahu): Sale of something the seller does not possess; considered invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Iraqi Hanafi scholars, when is the sale of a fish that has been caught and released into a tank permissible?
A) Only if the fish is never caught.
B) If the seller can recapture the fish without trapping.
C) Only if the buyer has seen the fish.
D) It is never permissible.

Key Takeaway
A valid sale requires both ownership and ability to deliver; an intra-Hanafi dispute exists on whether easy recapture suffices for delivery.

Sale of Fetus and Its Offspring: Gharar Invalidates
Stating the ruling that sales involving gharar are invalid, with examples of fetus sales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a fetus and its offspring and identify the hadith prohibition and the principle of gharar that render the sale batil.

Core Idea
Selling something uncertain like a fetus is batil – both the Prophet's prohibition and gharar invalidate the contract.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a foundational principle in Islamic commercial law: any sale involving gharar (uncertainty) is impermissible. The author illustrates this with the extreme cases of selling an unborn fetus and even the potential offspring of that fetus. Understanding this ruling helps you grasp the Hanafi strictness in ensuring that sale contracts are free from uncertainty that could lead to disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is selling the fetus (حمل) and its offspring (نتاج الحمل). The ruling is that such sales are not permissible; they are batil (void).
The passage explicitly states 'بيع ما فيه غرر لا يجوز' and then applies it to the fetus.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is a hadith: the Prophet prohibited the sale of the fetus (الحبل) and the fetus of a fetus (حبل الحبلة). This is cited in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and other sources.
The hadith is found in Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan al-Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative of prohibition (نهى) indicates that the act is prohibited (haram) and, in Hanafi fiqh, renders the contract batil. The explicit prohibition covers both the fetus and its offspring.
The Hanafi school holds that prohibitions in sales lead to batil, not just fasid, if the prohibition is directly on the subject matter.
4
Understand the gharar reasoning
Even without the hadith, the sale involves gharar because the existence and condition of the fetus are uncertain; the animal may not be pregnant. This uncertainty can lead to disputes, violating the principle of transparency.
The commentator mentions the possibility of bloating due to wind, highlighting the uncertainty.
5
Note the modern application
This principle applies to any sale where the object's existence or essential quality is unknown at contract time, such as selling crops before they are fully grown or goods not yet manufactured.
Salam (advance sale) is an exception because specifications eliminate uncertainty.

Principles of Hidayah, Third. (22) The sale of something containing gharar is not permissible. Translation: The sale of something in which there is deception is not permissible. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that any sale in which there is a strong possibility of deception is not permissible. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, is stating that selling the fetus (حمل) and similarly selling the offspring of the fetus (حمل الحبل - نتاج الحمل) is not permissible, because it is possible that there is no fetus in the animal's belly but rather it is bloated due to wind or some other cause. So in this sale there is deception, and every sale in which there is deception is not permissible. Therefore, the sale of the produce of a field and the sale of the offspring of the fetus are also not permissible. And if taken without it (meaning without a trick?), it is valid and he has the option due to the difference in value in water and outside it, and the sale of the bird in the air is not permissible before or after its catch and it does not return after its release, as previously mentioned in Al-Lubab. (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab). Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid. (His saying: 'and the fetus and the offspring') meaning their sale is not permissible. The fetus (الحمل) with sukoon on the meem is the embryo. And النتاج is the offspring of the pregnant animal (حمل الحبلة). The Prophet prohibited the sale of the fetus and the fetus of a fetus. The taa entered it to indicate femininity. It is said it means selling what the fetus will later carry.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with a proof from hadith. The principle is that any sale involving gharar (uncertainty/deception) is not permissible. The commentator uses the example of selling a fetus in an animal's womb, which is invalid because the existence and characteristics of the fetus are uncertain. The same applies to selling the offspring of a fetus (نتاج الحمل), which involves even greater uncertainty. The proof is the Prophet's explicit prohibition: 'عَنْ بَيْعِ الْحَبَلِ وَحَبَلِ الْحَبَلَةِ' (selling the fetus and the fetus of the fetus). This hadith is cited from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The sale is batil (void) due to both the prohibition and the existence of gharar. This reflects the Hanafi strict stance against uncertainty in contracts.

Key Terms
غرر (gharar): Uncertainty or deception that can lead to dispute; in this context, the uncertainty about the existence and condition of the fetus.
حمل (haml): The fetus in the womb of an animal or human; in the text, it refers specifically to the unborn offspring.
نتاج (nitaaj): The offspring of a pregnant animal, often used for the offspring of the fetus itself (حبل الحبلة).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The consensus of the Companions.
D) Istihsan based on necessity.

Key Takeaway
Selling a fetus or its offspring is batil because of the Prophet's explicit prohibition and the presence of gharar, establishing a key principle against uncertainty in sales.

The Prohibition of Selling with Gharar: Fetus Sales
Principle that gharar invalidates sale, applied to fetuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a fetus and identify the dalil that prohibits it.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if the subject matter is uncertain — Hanafis prohibit selling a fetus due to gharar and the Prophet's explicit prohibition.

This lesson examines the foundational Hanafi principle that any sale involving significant uncertainty (gharar) is invalid. The Hidayah applies this principle to the sale of an unborn animal (fetus) and even the fetus of the fetus, demonstrating how the rule operates in practice. By studying the prophetic proof and Hanafi reasoning, you will understand why such transactions are void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint what exactly is being sold (the fetus and the fetus of the fetus) and the legal classification (batil).
The ruling is explicit: the sale is not permissible and is void.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the Prophet's prohibition of selling al-habal and habal al-habalah.
This is a sunnah ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalalah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The prohibition (nahy) indicates impermissibility and invalidity (fasad/batil) in sales.
Hanafi usul: al-nahy fi al-mu'amalat yufid al-fasad.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Although Hanafis hold it batil absolutely, some other schools may allow it under certain conditions. Recognize the cross-madhhab dispute.
The mukhtalaf_fih status is noted in the source.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the sale is batil, based on the zahir al-riwayah and the general principle of gharar.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded here.

(22) Selling that which contains gharar is not permissible. Translation: The sale of an item in which there is deception is not permissible. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that a sale in which there is a strong fear of deception is not permissible. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the principle, explains that selling the fetus, and likewise selling the fetus of the fetus, is not permissible, because it is possible that the animal's womb does not contain a fetus but is swollen due to wind or some other cause. Thus, there is deception in this sale, and every sale in which there is deception is not permissible. Therefore, the sale of the fetus and the sale of the fetus of the fetus will also not be permissible. Al-habal is a verbal noun from habulat al-mar'atu habalan, so she is habla, and the carried thing is named after it, just as it is named al-haml. The ta' entered it to indicate feminine meaning. It is said its meaning is that he sells what the fetus will subsequently carry.)
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school stating the principle that any sale involving gharar (uncertainty) is not permissible. The author then applies this principle to the sale of an unborn animal (fetus) and the sale of the fetus of the fetus. The proof is the Prophet's prohibition of selling 'al-habal' (the fetus) and 'habal al-habalah' (the fetus of the fetus). The commentary explains that such sales are batil (void) because the existence of the fetus is uncertain; the animal may not be pregnant, and thus there is gharar. The text also mentions that if someone takes the goods without the prohibited sale, it is valid with an option, and analogizes to selling a bird in the air. This illustrates the Hanafi position that gharar invalidates a sale.

Key Terms
بَيْعُ مَا فِيهِ غَرَرٌ (bay'u ma fihi gharar): A sale that involves uncertainty or deception regarding the subject matter or price.
حمل (haml): Fetus (with sukoon on the meem); the unborn offspring of an animal.
حبل الحبلة (habal al-habalah): The fetus of the fetus (offspring of an unborn animal).
غَرَر (gharar): Uncertainty or risk that is significant and affects the validity of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school invalidates the sale of a fetus (haml) and the fetus of a fetus (habal al-habalah) due to gharar and the Prophet's prohibition.

Selling Subordinate Items Separately is Invalid
Ruling principle with two proofs and a qiyas distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling wool on a sheep and explain the two reasons for its invalidity.

Core Idea
Selling a subordinate attribute separately from its principal is invalid due to its nature as a description and resulting uncertainty.

This lesson explores a key principle in Hanafi sales law: a subordinate item (tabi') cannot be sold independently of its principal (matbu'). The classical example is selling the wool on a sheep's back without selling the sheep. The Hanafi school rules such a sale invalid (batil) for two distinct reasons rooted in the nature of the item and the certainty required in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling wool on the back of a sheep. The Hanafi ruling is that this sale is not permissible (la yajuz) and invalid (batil).
The ruling applies to any pure description attached to an animal.
2
Locate the dalil
The source cites two proofs: (1) wool is a pure description (wasf mahd), not an independent property; (2) wool grows from underneath causing mixture of sold and unsold items.
Both reasons are from the text of Al-Hidayah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for the first reason
Anything attached to an animal is considered a description, not a mal. A description cannot be sold separately because it has no independent legal status.
This distinguishes wool on an animal from fruit on a tree, which is a mal.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for the second reason
Wool grows from underneath, so new growth mixes with the sold item. This creates gharar (uncertainty) and leads to dispute over what was actually sold.
Mixing of non-sold with sold invalidates the contract.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
The ruling is mukhtalaf fih; some other schools may allow it if the wool is specified, but Hanafis prohibit absolutely.
This ikhtilaf is based on differing views on the legal status of attached attributes.

Source Text

ترجمہ: تابع کو بیع کے ذریعے الگ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو چیز تابع اور وصف ہو اس کو اصول کے بغیر الگ کر کے فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، مثلاً بھیڑ یا بکری وغیرہ کی صرف اون فروخت کرنا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ بکری اور بھیٹر وغیرہ کی پشت پر جو بال اور اون ہوتے ہیں، تنہا ان کی خرید و فروخت درست نہیں ہے، اس لیے کہ یہ حیوان کے تابع ہیں اور متبوع کے بغیر تابع کی کوئی حیثیت نہیں ہے، لہذا محض اس اون کا فروخت کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ نیز اون وغیرہ نیچے سے پیدا ہوتی ہے، اور وقتاً فوقتاً اس میں اضافہ ہوتا رہتا ہے، لہذا طبیع کا غیر مبیع سے اختلاط لازم آئے گا، اس لیے کہ مبیع تو وہ اون ہے جو بوقت بیع موجود تھی بعد میں بڑھنے والی اون اس میں شامل نہیں ، تو اب یہاں غیر مبیع کا مبیع
کے ساتھ اختلاط لازم آ رہا ہے جو مفسد عقد ہے۔ نیز اون کاٹنے کی جگہ غیر متعین ہے اس میں بھی تنازع واقع ہوگا۔
إن كان أنثى، وكانوا في الجاهلية يعتادون ذلك فأبطله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولأن فيه غررا وهو ما طوى عنك علمه. (العناية: كتاب البيوع، باب البيع الفاسد، ج ۶ ص ۴۱۱)
الهداية: كتاب البيوع، باب البیع الفاسد، ج ۳ ص ۵۳
وَبَيْعُ الصُّوفِ عَلَى ظَهْرِ الْغَنَمِ لَا يَجُوزُ لِوَجْهَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ بَابِ أَوْصَافِ الْحَيَوَانِ لأَنَّ مَا هُوَ مُتَّصِلْ بِالْحَيَوَانِ فَهُوَ وَصْفٌ مَحْضٌ بِخِلَافِ مَا يَكُونُ مُتَّصِلًا بِالشَّجَرِ فَإِنَّهُ عَيْنُ مَالٍ مَقْصُودٍ مِنْ وَجُهِ فَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُهُ، وَلَأَنَّهُ يَنْبُتُ مِنْ أَسْفَلَ فَيَخْتَلِطُ الْمَسِيعُ بِغَيْرِهِ وَهُوَ مُبْطِلٌ كَمَا مَرَّ : العناية: كتاب البيوع، باب البیع الفاسد، ج ۲ ص ۴۱۲)
(23) Isolating the subordinate by selling is not permissible. Translation: Selling the subordinate separately is not permissible. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that an item which is subordinate and a description cannot be sold separately without the principal, for example, selling only the wool of a sheep or goat. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that the hair and wool on the back of goats and sheep, their sale alone is not valid, because they are subordinate to the animal, and the subordinate has no status without the principal. Therefore, selling just that wool is not valid. Furthermore, wool grows from underneath, and it increases over time, so mixing of the sold item with non-sold item becomes necessary, because the sold item is the wool that existed at the time of sale; the subsequent growth is not included. Thus, mixing of non-sold with sold becomes necessary, which invalidates the contract. Also, the place of cutting the wool is undetermined, leading to dispute. (If it is female, and they used to do that in the Jahiliyyah, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) invalidated it, and because it contains gharar, which is what is hidden from your knowledge.) (Al-`Inayah: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 6, p. 411) Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 3, p. 53. (And selling wool on the back of sheep is not permissible for two reasons: because it is from the category of descriptions of animals, for whatever is attached to an animal is a pure description, unlike what is attached to a tree, for it is a sought-after property in some respect, so its sale is permissible. And because it grows from underneath, so the sold item mixes with other than it, and that invalidates, as has passed.) Al-`Inayah: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 2, p. 412)
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents the principle that a subordinate item (tabi') cannot be sold separately from its principal (matbu'). The example given is selling wool on the back of a sheep alone. The author provides two reasons: (1) the wool is a pure description (wasf) attached to the animal, and descriptions cannot be sold independently; (2) the wool grows from underneath, causing the sold item to mix with subsequent growth, leading to an invalid contract due to uncertainty (gharar). Additionally, the place of cutting is unspecified, leading to dispute. The text distinguishes wool on an animal from fruit on a tree, which can be sold separately because fruit is a sought-after property in its own right. This demonstrates the Hanafi school's emphasis on ensuring that the subject of sale is clearly defined and separate from non-sold items.

Key Terms
إِفْرَادُ التَّابِعِ بِالْبَيْعِ (ifrad al-tabi' bi al-bay'): Selling the subordinate item separately from the principal.
تابع (tabi'): Subordinate or attribute that is connected to the principal.
وصف (wasf): Attribute or description; something that is not a mal in itself.
صوف (suf): Wool; when attached to the animal it is considered a description, but once cut it becomes a mal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The wool is a description attached to the animal
B) The wool grows from underneath and mixes with non-sold items
C) Both A and B
D) Because the sheep may die before shearing

Key Takeaway
A subordinate attribute attached to an animal cannot be sold separately because it is a pure description and its growth creates uncertainty; thus the sale is batil.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Possession as a Trust Does Not Substitute for Possession as Sale
Distinction between trust and sale possession with rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between trust possession (qabd al-amanah) and sale possession (qabd al-bay') and apply the Hanafi rule that trust possession does not fulfill the requirement of sale possession.

Core Idea
Trust possession cannot substitute for sale possession because the weaker cannot stand in for the stronger in liability.

In this lesson, we examine a key principle of Hanafi sales law: the type of possession matters. Trust possession, which carries no liability for loss, cannot fulfill the requirement of possession in a sale, which requires liability. We will explore the rationale based on the strength of liability (daman) and work through a concrete example of a runaway slave to see how intention determines the nature of possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of possession
Define qabd al-amanah (trust possession) and qabd al-bay' (sale possession). Note their key difference: trust possession does not entail liability (daman) for loss unless negligence occurs, while sale possession entails full liability.
Trust possession is weak; sale possession is strong.
2
State the principle
The principle: the weaker cannot substitute for the stronger. Therefore, trust possession cannot stand in for sale possession. The legal effects are fundamentally different.
This is a rational (aqlī) proof based on the nature of liability.
3
Analyze the example of a runaway slave
Consider Zayd's runaway slave caught by Amr. If Amr declares his intention to return the slave (making witnesses), his possession is trust. Later, if Zayd sells the slave to Amr, that prior trust possession does NOT count as sale possession. A new, separate possession after the contract is required.
The intention at the time of taking possession determines its legal category.
4
Distinguish the practical consequence
If the slave is destroyed while in Amr's possession before the sale, Amr incurs no liability because it is trust. After the sale, Amr must take possession anew to transfer liability.
Liability (daman) flips from no liability to full liability upon taking sale possession.
5
Apply the rule to general cases
Whenever a person holds an item as a trust (e.g., found property, borrowed item), that possession does not count as sale possession for a subsequent purchase. The buyer must physically take the item with the intention of ownership.
This prevents ambiguity in risk allocation.

Source Text

(۲۴) قَبضُ الأَمَانَةِ لَا يَتُوبُ عَنْ قَبْضِ الْبَيْعِ. 0 ترجمہ: امانت کا قبضہ کرنا بیع کے قبضے کے قائم مقام نہیں ہوسکتا۔ تشریح مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امانت پر قبضہ کرنا بیع پر قبضہ کرنے کے قائم مقام اور نائب نہیں بن سکتا، اس لیے کہ مبیع کا قبضہ قوی ہے اور اس میں ہلاکت کی صورت میں ضمان آتا ہے اور امانت کا قبضہ ضعیف ہے اس میں ضمان نہیں ہوتا اور ادونی قوی کا قائم مقام نہیں بن سکتا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلار ہے ہیں کہ مثلاً اگر زید کا غلام بھاگ گیا اور عمرو نے اسے پکڑ لیا، اب اگر زید سے بیچنا چاہے تو اسے فروخت کر سکتا ہے، اس لیے کہ بھاگے ہوئے غلام کی بیچ اس لیے منع ہے کہ وہ غیر مقدور التسلیم ہوتا ہے، جب مشتری نے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا ہے تو اب اس کی پیچ درست ہے، اب آیا یہی قبضہ کافی ہے یا بیچ کے لیے الگ سے قبضہ ہوگا، تو اس میں تفصیل یہ ہے کہ اگر عمر و نے غلام پکڑتے وقت اس بات پر گواہ بنالیا تھا کہ میں اسے زید کو واپس کروں گا، تو اس صورت میں یہ قبضہ، قبضہ بیچ نہیں ہوگا بلکہ یہ قبضہ امانت ہوگا، اسی وجہ سے اگر یہ غلام زید کولوٹانے سے پہلے عمرو کے پاس ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس پر ضمان نہیں ہوگا، اس لیے کہ امانت اگر بغیر تعدی کے ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس پر ضمان نہیں آتا، تو پہلے والا قبضہ امانت ہے، اب بیع کے لیے جو قبضہ بعد العقد ہو گا وہ قبضہ بیع کہلائے گا، (قَوْلُهُ وَلَا الصُّوفَ عَلَى ظَهْرِ الْغَنَمِ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ أَوْصَافِ الْحَيَوَانِ، لِأَنَّهُ يَقُومُ بِهِ أَوْ لأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ الْمَقْصُودِ مِنْ الشَّاةِ فَكَانَ كَالْوَصْفِ مِنَ الذَّاتِ وَهُوَ لَا يُفْرَدُ بِالْبَيْعِ (وَلَأَنَّهُ يَنْبُتُ مِنْ أَسْفَلَ سَاعَةً فَسَاعَةً فَيَخْتَلِطُ الْمَبِيعُ بِغَيْرِهِ) بِحَيْثُ يَتَعَذَّرُ التَّمْيِيزُ . فتح القدير : كتاب البيوع، باب البیع الفاسد، ج ۶ ص ۴۱۱) الهداية كتاب البيوع، باب البيع الفاسد ج ۳ ص ۵۶
Rule 24: Possession of a trust does not substitute for possession of a sale. Translation: Taking possession as a trust cannot stand in place of taking possession in a sale. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that taking possession of a thing as a trust cannot be the substitute or deputy for taking possession in a sale, because possession of the sold item is strong and involves liability in case of destruction, while trust possession is weak and does not involve liability, and the weaker cannot substitute for the stronger. The author of Al-Hidayah, mentioning the principle, explains that for example, if Zayd's slave runs away and Amr catches him, now if Zayd wants to sell him, he can sell him, because selling a runaway slave is prohibited due to inability to deliver, but when the buyer has taken possession, the sale is valid. Now, whether this same possession is sufficient or a separate possession is needed for the sale? The detail is: if Amr at the time of catching the slave made witnesses that he will return him to Zayd, then this possession is not possession of sale but possession of trust. Therefore, if the slave dies with Amr before returning, no liability (ضمان) is incurred, because if a trust is destroyed without transgression, no liability is incurred. So the first possession is a trust, and the possession that occurs after the contract for the sale will be called possession of sale. (His statement: And not the wool on the back of sheep because it is from the descriptions of animals, because it subsists by it, or because it is not the intended object from the sheep, so it is like a description of the essence, and it is not sold separately; and because it grows from below moment by moment, so the sold mixes with other [wool] such that differentiation becomes impossible. Fath al-Qadir: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 6 p. 411. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 3 p. 56)
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage establishes a legal principle in Hanafi fiqh regarding possession (قبض). The core idea is that the nature of possession matters: trust possession (قبض الأمانة) is weak and does not entail liability (ضمان) for loss, whereas sale possession (قبض البيع) is strong and entails liability. Therefore, the weak cannot substitute for the strong. The text provides a detailed example of a runaway slave: if a person catches a runaway slave with the intention of returning him (thus holding him in trust), that possession does not count as possession for a subsequent sale. The buyer must take a new, distinct possession after the sale contract to transfer liability. This distinction prevents the mixing of legal categories and ensures clarity in contractual obligations. The passage also quotes a related discussion from Fath al-Qadir and Al-Hidayah about selling wool, reinforcing the principle that dependent descriptions cannot be sold separately.

Key Terms
قبض الأمانة (qabd al-amanah): Possession taken without liability for loss, typically for safekeeping or return.
قبض البيع (qabd al-bay'): Possession taken under a sale contract, which transfers liability for loss to the buyer.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Trust possession (qabd al-amanah) cannot substitute for sale possession (qabd al-bay') because the weaker cannot stand in for the stronger; a new, distinct possession with ownership intention is required for a valid sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Trust Possession Does Not Substitute for Sale Possession
Principle 24 from Usool al-Hidayah with example of absconding slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that trust possession does not substitute for sale possession and apply it to determine whether prior possession suffices in a sale contract.

Core Idea
A weaker possession (trust) cannot replace a stronger possession (sale) because liability differs.

In Hanafi sales law, not all forms of possession are equal. This lesson introduces a key principle from al-Hidayah: possession held as a trust (amānah) does not count as possession for a sale contract. The reason lies in the presence or absence of liability (ḍamān). Understanding this distinction is critical for determining when a buyer's prior holding of an item fulfills the delivery requirement.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle and its rationale
First, grasp the maxim: trust possession cannot substitute for sale possession. This is because sale possession is strong (qawī) as it carries liability for destruction, while trust possession is weak (ḍaʿīf) without liability (absent negligence). The weaker cannot replace the stronger.
This is a legal maxim, not a hukm taklifi. It governs the classification of possession.
2
Identify the two types of possession
Distinguish between trust possession (qabḍ al-amānah) and sale possession (qabḍ al-bayʿ). Trust possession arises from contracts like wadiʿah or ʿāriyah, where the holder is not liable for loss. Sale possession arises from a valid sale contract and imposes liability on the buyer.
A third type, ghaṣb (usurpation), also carries liability and is treated like sale possession.
3
Recognize the exception: ghaṣb possession equals sale possession
If the prior possession was through ghaṣb (without witness of intent to return), it carries liability just like sale possession. Therefore, it can substitute for sale possession. The passage illustrates this with the example of a runaway slave.
The key factor is liability: if liability attaches, the possession is strong enough to substitute.
4
Apply to the runaway slave example
Consider Zayd's slave runs away; ʿAmr catches him. If ʿAmr witnesses that he intends to return the slave to Zayd, his possession is trust (amānah). If he later buys the slave, he must take fresh possession after the contract. If ʿAmr does not witness (i.e., he takes as a usurper), his possession is ghaṣb, which suffices for sale possession.
The detail hinges on the presence of a witness regarding intention to return.
5
Determine the ruling in similar scenarios
Use the principle to analyze analogous cases: e.g., a borrower later buys the borrowed item, or a finder of lost property later purchases it. The prior trust possession does not count; a new delivery is required unless the prior possession was ghaṣb.
This ensures the sale is valid with proper delivery (taslīm) as required by Hanafi law.

اصول ہدایہ ثالث
۵۴
چونکہ قبضہ بیع میں اگر مبیع مشتری کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس پر ضمان آتا ہے، تو یہ قبضہ قوی ہوا، اور قبضہ امانت میں چونکہ ضمان نہیں آتا اس لیے وہ ادنی ہے، اقوی ادنی کا نائب ہوسکتا ہے لیکن ادنی اقوی کا نائب نہیں بن سکتا، تو امانت کا قبضہ ادنی ہے اس لیے وہ بیع اقوی کے نائب نہیں ہو سکتا ، اب مشتری کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ وہ از سر نو اس غلام پر قبضہ کرے۔ اور اگر عمر و ( مشتری) نے غلام کو پکڑتے وقت اس کے مولی کی طرف واپس کرنے کے متعلق گواہ وغیرہ نہیں بنایا تو اس صورت میں اس کا یہ قبضہ، قبضہ بیع کے قائم مقام ہوگا، اس لیے کہ یہ قبضہ، قبضہ غصب ہے، جس طرح قبضہ بیچ میں ضمان آتا ہے، اسی طرح قبضہ غصب میں بھی ضمان آتا ہے، لہذا دونوں قبضے برابر ہیں، کسی ایک کو دوسرے پر فوقیت نہیں ہے، اس لیے کہ دونوں میں ضمان آتا ہے، اس لیے مشتری کا قبضہ اولی ہی کافی ہو گا، اس لیے اس غلام کو بائع کی طرف واپس کر کے از سر نو قبضہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
(قَوْلُهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَبِيعَهُ مِمَّنْ يَزْعُمُ أَنَّهُ عِنْدَهُ) فَيَجُوزُ الْبَيْعُ لِأَنَّ الْمَنْهِيَّ عَنْهُ بَيْعُ آبِقٍ مُطْلَقٍ، وَهُوَ أَنْ يَكُونَ آبِقًا فِي حَقِّهِمَا، وَهَذَا غَيْرُ آبِقٍ فِي حَقِّ الْمُشْتَرِي، وَلَأَنَّهُ إِذَا كَانَ عِندَ الْمُشْتَرِى انْتَفَى العَجْرُ عَنْ التَّسْلِيمِ، وَهُوَ الْمَانِعُ، وَلَمْ يَذْكُرُ الْمُصَنِّفُ أَنَّهُ يَكْتَفِي بِقَبْضِهِ عَنْ قَبْضِ الْمَبِيعِ لِلتَّفْصِيلِ قَالُوا إِنْ كَانَ أَشْهَدَ وَقْتَ أَخْذِهِ أَنَّهُ أَخَذَهُ لِيَرُدَّهُ عَلَى مَالِكِهِ كَانَ أَمَانَةٌ فِي يَدِهِ فَلَا يَنُوبُ عَنْ قَبْضِ الْبَيْعِ فَلَوْ هَلَكَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَصِلَ إِلَى سَيِّدِهِ لَمْ يَضْمَنْهُ فَيَنْفَسِحُ الْبَيْعُ، وَيَرْجِعُ عَلَى سَيِّدِهِ بِالشَّمَنِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ لَمْ يُشْهِدُ صَارَ قَابِضًا لأنَّهُ قَبضُ غَصْبٍ. (البحر الرائق: كتاب البيوع، باب البيع الفاسد، ج ۶ ص ۸۷)
قال ولا يجوز بيع الآبق) بيع الآبق المطلق لا يجوز لما ذكر محمد في الأصل بقوله بلغنا عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن بيع الغرر وعن بيع
Principles of Hidayah Third Volume 53 (24) The possession of a trust does not substitute for the possession of a sale. Translation: Possession by trust cannot stand in place of possession by sale. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that possession by trust cannot act as a substitute or deputy for possession by sale, because the possession of the sold item is strong and entails liability (daman) in case of destruction, whereas possession by trust is weak and does not entail liability. The weaker cannot stand in place of the stronger. The author of Hidayah states this principle and explains: For example, if Zayd's slave runs away and Amr catches him, then if Zayd wants to sell him, he may sell, because selling a runaway slave is prohibited only when he is not deliverable. Since the buyer has taken possession, the sale is valid. Now, is this possession sufficient or is separate possession required for the sale? The detail is: if Amr had witnesses at the time of taking that he would return him to Zayd, then this possession is trust, not sale possession. Consequently, if the slave dies before being returned, Amr is not liable, because trust without negligence does not incur liability. So the initial possession is trust, and the possession after the contract will be sale possession. (His statement: "And not the wool on the back of the sheep" because it is among the characteristics of the animal, because it grows on it, or because it is not the primary purpose of the sheep, so it is like a characteristic of the essence and is not sold separately, and because it grows from below hour by hour, so the sold item mixes with others such that distinction becomes impossible. Fath al-Qadir: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 6 p. 411. Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 3 p. 56.) Principles of Hidayah Third Volume 54 Since in sale possession, if the sold item is destroyed in the buyer's hands, liability applies, so this possession is strong. In trust possession, since liability does not apply, it is weaker. The stronger can be a substitute for the weaker, but the weaker cannot be a substitute for the stronger. Thus, trust possession is weaker, so it cannot substitute for sale possession. Therefore, the buyer must take possession of the slave anew. If Amr (the buyer) did not have witnesses regarding returning to the master, then his possession stands in place of sale possession, because this possession is wrongful (ghasb) possession. Just as sale possession entails liability, so does ghasb possession. Hence, the two possessions are equal; neither has superiority over the other because both entail liability. Therefore, the buyer's initial possession suffices, and there is no need to return the slave to the seller and take possession anew. (His statement: "Unless he sells him to someone who claims that he is with him" then the sale is permissible because the prohibited thing is the sale of an absolute runaway, meaning it is a runaway with respect to both parties, and this slave is not a runaway with respect to the buyer. And because when he is with the buyer, inability to deliver is removed, which is the impediment. The author did not mention that his possession suffices for possession of the sold item because of the detail. They said: If he had witnesses at the time of taking that he took it to return to its owner, then it is a trust in his hand and does not substitute for sale possession. So if it perishes before reaching its master, he does not guarantee it, so the sale is annulled and he recovers the price from the master. If he did not have witnesses, he becomes a possessor because it is ghasb possession. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 6 p. 87) He said: "And the sale of a runaway is not permissible" The sale of an absolute runaway is not permissible, as Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl, saying: We were told that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of gharar and the sale of...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from Usool al-Hidayah presents principle number (24): 'The possession of a trust does not substitute for the possession of a sale.' The author explains that possession by trust (amanah) is inherently weaker than possession by sale (bay') because sale possession carries liability (daman) if the item is destroyed, while trust possession does not (unless there is negligence). Therefore, the weaker cannot replace the stronger. The example of a runaway slave illustrates this: if a buyer already holds the slave as a trust (intending to return him), that possession does not count as sale possession, and a new possession after the contract is required. However, if the buyer holds the slave as a usurper (ghasb), the possession is equivalent to sale possession because both entail liability. The passage then quotes from Fath al-Qadir about the sale of wool on sheep, and from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq regarding the detail of the runaway slave. Finally, a brief statement from al-Hidayah is given: the absolute sale of a runaway is prohibited due to the prohibition of gharar. This principle is critical for understanding how possession affects the validity of a sale contract in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
قبض (qabḍ): Physical possession or taking control of an item; in this context, the act of taking possession that determines the legal nature of the holding.
أمانة (amānah): Possession under a trust arrangement where the holder is not liable for loss unless negligent.
غصب (ghaṣb): Wrongful possession or usurpation; the holder is liable for the item and its benefits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does trust possession (qabḍ al-amānah) not substitute for sale possession (qabḍ al-bayʿ)?
A) Because trust possession is stronger than sale possession.
B) Because trust possession entails liability while sale possession does not.
C) Because trust possession is weaker and does not carry liability, while sale possession does.
D) Because trust possession only applies to movable items.

Key Takeaway
Trust possession lacks liability and thus cannot substitute for sale possession; only possession with liability (like ghasb) can.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Possession by Usurpation Substitutes for Possession of Sale
Explains the Hanafi principle that possession by usurpation can substitute for possession of sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that possession by usurpation substitutes for possession of sale, explain the rationale based on liability (daman), and apply it to determine when a prior possession suffices for a subsequent purchase.

Core Idea
Possession with liability (ghasb) equals sale possession; trust possession (amana) is weaker and cannot substitute.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi principle in sales law: the substitution of possession. The presence of liability (daman) determines the strength of possession. Trust possession (amana) lacks liability, thus it cannot stand in place of the strong possession required in a sale. The passage from al-Hidayah and its commentaries illustrates this through the case of a runaway slave, showing how the buyer's prior possession, if held as a ghasb, eliminates the need for a new physical takeover after purchase.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific ruling being proved? The sale of a slave that was previously in the buyer's possession as a ghasb is valid without fresh possession.
The ruling is about the sufficiency of prior possession.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the prohibition of gharar (uncertainty). The hadith ‘The Prophet forbade the sale of gharar’ implies that delivery must be possible; if the slave is already with the buyer, inability to deliver is removed.
The dalil is a hadith with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The presence of liability (daman) in both ghasb possession and sale possession makes them equivalent. Since the ghasb possessor is liable for destruction just like a buyer, the prior possession is sufficient.
Liability is the common effective cause (illa) for the substitution.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (Shafi'i, etc.) may not accept this substitution, but within the Hanafi school it is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
This ikhtilaf is legitimate.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is upheld by the commentators of al-Hidayah as the soundest view.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the proof and acceptance by the majority of Hanafi jurists.

(البحر الرائق: كتاب البيوع، باب البيع الفاسد، ج ۶ ص ۸۷)
قال ولا يجوز بيع الآبق) بيع الآبق المطلق لا يجوز لما ذكر محمد في الأصل بقوله بلغنا عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نه نهى عن بيع الغرر وعن بيع

اصول ہدایہ ثالث
(۲۵) قَبْضُ الْعَصَبِ يَنُوبُ عَنْ قَبْضِ الْبَيْعِ. ترجمہ: غصب کا قبصہ بیع کے قبضے کا قائم مقام ہو سکتا ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ غاصب کا قبضہ یہ مشتری کے قبضے کے مانند ہے، کیونکہ ان دونوں میں مبیع کی ہلاکت کی صورت میں ضمان آتا ہے، لہذا یہ دونوں مماثل اور قوی ہیں اور ایک قومی دوسرے قومی کے قائم مقام ہو سکتا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ مذکورہ بالا صورت میں اگر مشتری نے غلام کو پکڑتے وقت بائع کی طرف لوٹانے کے لیے گواہ قائم نہیں کیسے تھے، تو یہ قبضہ، قبضہ غصب ہوگا ، اب اگر یہ قابض (مشتری) اس غلام کو خرید لے تو اس پر جدید قبضے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، بلکہ صرف عقد سے یہ قابض شمار ہوگا، کیونکہ مذکورہ صورت میں مشتری کا پہلا قبضہ، قبضہ غصب تھا اور قبضہ غصب قبضہ بالبیع کا قائم مقام ہو سکتا ہے، لہذا مشتری کا پہلا قبضہ، قبضہ بالغصب دوسرے قبضہ یعنی قبضہ بالبیع کا قائم مقام ہوگا اور از سر نو
العبد الآبق ولأنه غير مقدور التسليم والآبق الذى لا يكون مطلقا وهو الذي لا يكون آبقا في حق أحد المتعاقدين جاز بيعه كمن باعه من رجل يزعم أنه عنده لأن المنهى عنه بيع المطلق منه، وهذا غير آبق فى حق المشترى فينتفى العجز عن التسليم المانع من الجواز ، ثم هل يصير قابضا بمجرد العقد أو لا، إن كان قبضه لنفسه يصير قابضا عقب الشراء بالاتفاق، وإن قبضه للرد فإما أن يشهد على ذلك أو لا، فإن كان الأول لا يصير قابضا لأنه أمانة عنده، حتى لو هلک قبل الوصول إلى المولى هلک من مال المولى وقبض الأمانة لا ينوب عن قبض البيع لأن قبض الضمان أقوى لتأكده باللزوم والملك. (العناية: كتاب البيوع، باب البيع الفاسد، ج ۶ ص ۴۲۱)
الهداية: كتاب البيوع، باب البیع الفاسد، ج ۳ ص ۵۶
Because in possession of sale, if the sold item is destroyed while with the buyer, liability (daman) falls on him, so this possession is strong. And in possession of trust (amana), since there is no liability, it is inferior. The stronger can deputize for the weaker, but the weaker cannot deputize for the stronger. So possession of trust is inferior, thus it cannot deputize for the stronger possession of sale. Now it is necessary for the buyer to take fresh possession of the slave. But if Amr (the buyer) did not appoint witnesses at the time of taking the slave regarding returning it to his master, then in that case his possession will stand in place of possession of sale, because this possession is possession by usurpation (qabd al-ghasb). Just as liability occurs in possession of sale, similarly liability occurs in possession by usurpation. Therefore, both possessions are equal; neither has superiority over the other because both entail liability. So the buyer's first possession suffices, and there is no need to return the slave to the seller and take fresh possession.
(His saying: 'Except if he sells it to someone who claims that it is with him') So the sale is permissible because the prohibited thing is the sale of an absolute runaway (abiq mutlaq), which is that it is a runaway with respect to both parties. And this is not a runaway with respect to the buyer. Also, because if it is with the buyer, the inability to deliver (which is the preventing factor) is removed. The author did not mention that his possession suffices for possession of the sold item due to detail. They said: If he appointed witnesses at the time of taking it that he took it to return it to its owner, then it is a trust (amana) in his hand, so it does not stand in place of possession of sale. If it is destroyed before reaching its master, he does not guarantee it, so the sale is rescinded, and he reclaims the price from its master. But if he did not appoint witnesses, he becomes a possessor (qabid) because it is possession by usurpation. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 6, p. 87)
He said: 'The sale of a runaway slave is not permissible.' The sale of an absolute runaway is not permissible due to what Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl: 'It has reached us from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he forbade the sale of gharar and the sale of...'

Usool-e-Hidayah vol. 3
(25) Possession by usurpation can stand in place of possession of sale. Translation: Possession by usurpation can serve as a substitute for possession of sale.
Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that the possessor's possession is like the buyer's possession because in both cases liability arises upon destruction of the sold item. Therefore, these two are similar and strong, and one strong can stand in place of another strong.
The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, is explaining that in the above case, if the buyer did not appoint witnesses at the time of taking the slave to return to the seller, then this possession is possession by usurpation. Now if this possessor (the buyer) buys this slave, he does not need fresh possession; rather, by mere contract he becomes a possessor, because in the aforementioned case the buyer's first possession was possession by usurpation, and possession by usurpation can stand in place of possession by sale. So the buyer's first possession (by usurpation) will stand in place of the second possession (by sale), so no fresh possession is needed.
The runaway slave and because it is not within the power to deliver. And the runaway that is not absolute, i.e., which is not a runaway in the right of either contracting party, its sale is permissible. Like one who sells it to a man who claims it is with him, because the prohibited thing is the sale of the absolute type, and this is not a runaway in the right of the buyer, so the inability to deliver (which prevents permissibility) is removed. Then, does he become a possessor merely by the contract or not? If his possession was for himself, he becomes a possessor immediately after purchase by agreement. If he took possession for return, then either he appoints witnesses for that or not. If the former, he does not become a possessor because it is a trust with him, so if it perishes before reaching the master, it perishes from the master's property. And possession of trust does not stand in place of possession of sale, because possession with liability is stronger due to its being confirmed by obligation and ownership. (Al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 6, p. 421)
Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Buyu', Bab al-Bay' al-Fasid, vol. 3, p. 56
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of a Hanafi legal principle: 'Possession by usurpation (qabd al-ghasb) can substitute for possession of sale (qabd al-bay')'. The Urdu commentary, drawing from al-Hidayah and its commentaries (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-'Inayah), explains the underlying reasoning based on the presence of liability (daman). The key insight is that both sale possession and ghasb possession entail liability on the possessor if the item is destroyed, making them equally 'strong'. In contrast, trust possession (amana) has no liability, making it 'weak' and thus unable to substitute for the stronger forms. The text applies this to a scenario of selling a runaway slave: if the buyer already holds the slave without witnesses indicating an intent to return it, his possession is deemed ghasb, and upon purchasing, his prior possession suffices—no new physical takeover is needed. If he did have witnesses, it is amana, and a new possession is required for the sale to be valid. The passage thus clarifies a nuanced area of Hanafi sales law, emphasizing the role of intent and formalities in determining the legal nature of possession.

Key Terms
قَبْضُ الْغَصْبِ (qabd al-ghasb): Possession of an item by usurpation, without the owner's consent, entailing liability for its destruction.
قَبْضُ الْبَيْعِ (qabd al-bay'): Possession taken by the buyer in a valid sale, transferring ownership and risk.
أَمَانَة (amānah): A trust; possession without liability, e.g., when someone takes an item with the intention to return it to the owner.
ضَمَان (ḍamān): Liability or guarantee; the obligation to compensate for loss or destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a buyer's prior possession of a slave (taken before purchase) count as valid possession for the sale, eliminating the need for a new takeover?
A) Only if he had witnesses that he took it to return to the seller.
B) Only if he did not have witnesses (making it ghasb).
C) Always, regardless of witnesses.
D) Never; a new possession is always required.

Key Takeaway
The presence of liability (daman) makes a possession strong enough to substitute for sale possession; trust possession cannot.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
